Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
6 min
The Imam's Sermon on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah
Prescribing the imam's sermon to teach pilgrimage rites

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of the imam's sermon on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah and identify its evidence from the sunnah.

Core Idea
The imam's sermon on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah is a sunnah to teach pilgrims the rites of Hajj before they begin.

This passage describes a recommended practice for the imam (or leader) of the Hajj caravan. On the 7th of Dhul Hijjah, the day before Yawm al-Tarwiyah, the imam delivers a sermon teaching the pilgrims the key rites: going out to Mina, prayer at 'Arafat, standing at 'Arafah, and the ifadah. This teaching is based on the Prophet's own practice, as recorded in the hadith of Ibn 'Umar. Understanding this sunnah helps us appreciate the educational aspect of Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the imam's sermon on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah. The ruling is sunnah muakkadah (highly recommended).
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence is the hadith of Ibn 'Umar that the Prophet would deliver such a sermon before Yawm al-Tarwiyah.
The hadith is narrated in Bayhaqi and Nasa'i.
3
Analyze the dalil
The phrase 'fakbarahum bi manasikihim' (informed them of their rites) shows the content. The consistent practice indicates sunnah.
The Prophet's action is a model (uswah).
4
Determine the time and content
The sermon is on the 7th, not Yawm al-Tarwiyah itself. Content includes going to Mina, prayer at 'Arafat, wuquf, and tawaf al-ifadah.
The passage lists four specific teachings.
5
Note the Hanafi position
It is sunnah, not wajib. Some schools may differ, but the Hanafi school relies on this hadith as sufficient evidence for recommendation.
Authority weight: zahir riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۶۴۰ (۳۶) اور جبکہ یوم ترویہ سے ایک دن پہلے ہو تو امام خطبہ دے گا ایسا خطبہ کہ لوگوں کو اس میں سکھلائیں گے منی کی طرف نکلنا اور عرفات میں نماز اور وقوف عرفہ اور افاضہ کے احکام۔ تش یوم ترویہ آٹھویں ذی الحجہ کو کہتے ہیں۔ اس سے ایک دن قبل ساتویں ذی الحجہ ہوگی۔ تو ساتویں ذی الحجہ کو امام خطبہ دے جس میں لوگوں کو منی کی طرف نکلنے کے احکام، عرفات میں نماز کے احکام سکھلائے۔ اسی طرح وقوف عرفہ کس طرح کریں ، طواف وداع کس طرح کریں یہ سب احکام سکھلا ئیں۔ ان احکام کے سکھلانے کی ضروت ہے اس لئے یہ احکام سکھلائے (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن ابن عمر قال كان رسول الله لا اذا كان قبل التروية خطب الناس فاخبرهم بمناسكهم (ج) ( سنن بیھقی ، باب الخطبة التي يستحب للامام ان یاتی بھائی الحج اولھا یوم السابع ج خامس ص ۱۸۰، نمبر ۹۴۳۶ رنسائی شریف، الخطبة قبل یوم الترویہ ج ثانی ص ۳۴ نمبر ۲۹۹۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ذی الحجہ کی ساتویں تاریخ کو خطبہ دینا چاہئے اور اس میں مناسک حج کے تمام پہلوا جاگر کرنا چاہئے۔
[640] (36) And when it is the day before Yawm al-Tarwiyah, the imam delivers a sermon in which he teaches the people the rulings about going out to Mina, prayer at 'Arafat, the standing (wuquf), and the ifadah. Yawm al-Tarwiyah is the 8th of Dhul Hijjah. One day before it is the 7th of Dhul Hijjah. So on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah, the imam delivers a sermon in which he teaches the people the rulings of going out to Mina, the rulings of prayer at 'Arafat, similarly how to perform wuquf at 'Arafah, how to perform tawaf al-ifadah – he teaches all these rulings. There is a need to teach these rulings, so he teaches them. (2) In a hadith: from Ibn 'Umar who said: 'The Messenger of Allah (ﷺ), when it was before Yawm al-Tarwiyah, delivered a sermon to the people and informed them about their rites (manasik).' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on the sermon that the imam should deliver at the beginning of Hajj on the seventh day, vol. 5, p. 180, no. 9436; Nasa'i, chapter on sermon before Yawm al-Tarwiyah, vol. 2, p. 34, no. 2996). This hadith shows that a sermon should be given on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah, and in it all the rites of Hajj should be explained.
Source pages p. 403

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement about the imam's responsibility to educate the pilgrims before the main days of Hajj. On the 7th of Dhul Hijjah, the day before Yawm al-Tarwiyah (8th), the imam (or the leader of the Hajj caravan) is to deliver a sermon teaching the people the rites they will soon perform. Specifically, he explains: going out to Mina, the prayer at 'Arafat, the standing at 'Arafah (wuquf), and the ifadah (which includes tawaf al-ifadah and the sacrifice). The author notes that this is necessary because pilgrims need to know the correct procedure. The evidence is the practice of the Prophet ﷺ as narrated by Ibn 'Umar: the Prophet would give such a sermon before Yawm al-Tarwiyah. Thus, this sermon is a recommended sunnah for the imam to perform.

Key Terms
يوم التروية (Yawm al-Tarwiyah): The 8th of Dhul Hijjah; named because pilgrims used to give water to their camels and prepare for the journey to Mina.
الافاضة (al-ifadah): The departure from 'Arafat to Muzdalifah and then to Mina for the sacrifice, including tawaf al-ifadah; generally refers to the flow of pilgrims from 'Arafat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
On which date does the imam deliver the sermon teaching the rites of Hajj according to this passage?
A) 8th of Dhul Hijjah (Yawm al-Tarwiyah)
B) 7th of Dhul Hijjah
C) 9th of Dhul Hijjah (Yawm 'Arafah)
D) 10th of Dhul Hijjah (Yawm al-Nahr)

Key Takeaway
The imam's sermon on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah is a sunnah to teach pilgrims the rites of Hajj before they begin, based on the Prophet's consistent practice.

The Imam's Teaching Sermon Before Yawm al-Tarwiyah
Ruling statement on the imam's teaching sermon before Yawm al-Tarwiyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the imam's sermon on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah and explain its basis in the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
The imam's sermon on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah is a confirmed sunnah, not an obligation.

This lesson covers a specific sunnah of Hajj: the imam delivering a teaching sermon on the day before Yawm al-Tarwiyah (7th Dhul Hijjah). The purpose is to instruct pilgrims in the upcoming rituals. The ruling is based on the practice of the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) as reported by Ibn Umar. We will examine the textual evidence and the Hanafi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its timing
The text specifies a sermon delivered by the imam one day before Yawm al-Tarwiyah, which is the 8th of Dhul Hijjah. So the sermon is on the 7th.
Yawm al-Tarwiyah is the day pilgrims prepare water and travel to Mina.
2
Determine the ruling level
The text does not use an imperative; it describes a practice. The commentary and hadith indicate it is a sunnah, not fard or wajib.
Hanafi usul: a prophetic action that is not commanded is generally a sunnah.
3
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith from Ibn Umar: 'When it was before al-Tarwiyah, the Prophet would deliver a sermon and inform them of their rituals.' This is a sound ahad hadith.
The reference: Sunan al-Bayhaqi and Sunan al-Nasa'i.
4
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's consistent action establishes a recommended practice. Since he did not command it, the Hanafi school classifies it as sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah).
Contrast with obligatory acts which are established by a direct command.
5
Note the cross-madhhab status
While the Hanafi school views this as sunnah, other schools may differ on the level of obligation. The practical difference is minimal since it is recommended.
The sermon is a mercy and a teaching tool, not a legal requirement for validity of Hajj.

Source Text

طاف بالبيت خمسين مرة خرج من ذنوبه كيوم ولدته امه (الف) ( ترمذی شریف ، باب ما جاء فی فضل الطواف ص ۷۵ انمبر ۸۶۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ طواف کا ثواب بہت ہے اس لئے زیادہ سے زیادہ طواف کرتا رہے اور حج کے احرام باندھنے والے کو محرم ہو کر رہنے کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے عن عائشة انها قالت خرجنا مع رسول الله عام حجة الوداع فمنا من اهل بعمرة ومنا من اهل بحج وعمرة ومنا من اهل بالحج واهل رسول الله الا الله بالحج فاما من اهل بعمرة فحل واما من اهل بحج او جمع الحج والعمرة فلم يحلوا حتى كان يوم النحر (ب) ( سنن بیھقی ، باب المفرد تقيم على احرامه حتى يتخلل منه يوم النخرج خامس ص ۱۷۸، نمبر ۹۴۲۸) اس منہ حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ جس نے حج کا احرام باندھایا حج اور عمرہ دونوں کا احرام باندھ کر قرآن کیا وہ طواف قدوم کے بعد احرام نہیں کھولے گا۔ بلکہ مکہ مکرمہ میں محرم ہو کر ٹھہرے گا۔ البتہ جس نے عمرہ کا احرام باندھا اس کا عمرہ پورا ہو جائے گا۔ اس لئے وہ احرام کھول دے گا اور حلالی ہو کر مکہ مکرمہ میں قیام کرے گا ۔ (۱۴۰) (۳۶) اور جبکہ یوم ترویہ سے ایک دن پہلے ہو تو امام خطبہ دے گا ایسا خطبہ کہ لوگوں کو اس میں سکھلائیں گے منی کی طرف نکلنا اور عرفات میں نماز اور وقوف عرفہ اور افاضہ کے احکام۔ تش یوم ترویہ آٹھویں ذی الحجہ کو کہتے ہیں۔ اس سے ایک دن قبل ساتویں ذی الحجہ ہوگی۔ تو ساتویں ذی الحجہ کو امام خطبہ دے جس میں لوگوں کو منی کی طرف نکلنے کے احکام، عرفات میں نماز کے احکام سکھلائے۔ اسی طرح وقوف عرفہ کس طرح کریں ، طواف وداع کس طرح کریں یہ سب احکام سکھلا ئیں۔ صلى الله (1) ان احکام کے سکھلانے کی ضروت ہے اس لئے یہ احکام سکھلائے (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن ابن عمر قال كان رسول الله لا اذا كان قبل التروية خطب الناس فاخبرهم بمناسكهم (ج) ( سنن بیھقی ، باب الخطبة التي يستحب للامام ان یاتی بھائی الحج اولھا یوم السابع ج خامس ص ۱۸۰، نمبر ۹۴۳۶ رنسائی شریف، الخطبة قبل یوم الترویہ ج ثانی ص ۳۴ نمبر ۲۹۹۶) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ذی الحجہ کی ساتویں تاریخ کو خطبہ دینا چاہئے اور اس میں مناسک حج کے تمام پہلوا جاگر کرنا چاہئے ۔ الا فاضہ : عرفات میں ٹھہرنے کو اور طواف فرض کو افاضہ کہتے ہیں۔ حاشیہ : (الف) آپ نے فرمایا جس نے پچاس مرتبہ بیت اللہ کا طواف کیا گناہ سے اس طرح نکل جائے گا جیسے آج ہی اس کی ماں نے جنا ہو (ب) حضرت عائشہ فرماتی ہیں کہ ہم حضور کے ساتھ حجتہ الوداع کے دن نکلے تو ہم میں سے کچھ نے عمرہ کا احرام باندھا اور ہم میں سے کچھ نے حج اور عمرہ کا احرام باندھا۔ اور ہم میں سے کچھ نے حج کا احرام باندھا۔ اور حضور نے حج کا احرام باندھا۔ پس جس نے عمرہ کا احرام باندھا وہ حلال ہو گیا۔ اور جس نے حج کا احرام باندھا یا حج اور عمرے کو جمع کیا تو وہ حلال نہیں ہوئے یہاں تک کہ دسویں تاریخ ہوگئی (ج) حضور نے آٹھویں تاریخ سے پہلے لوگوں کو خطبہ دیا اور ان کو ان کے مناسک حج کے بارے میں خبر دی۔
And when it is the day before Yawm al-Tarwiyah, the imam delivers a sermon teaching the people about going out to Mina, prayer at Arafat, standing (wuquf), and ifadah (departure). [Urdu commentary follows]
Source pages p. 403

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling: the imam should deliver a sermon on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah (the day before Yawm al-Tarwiyah) to teach the pilgrims the rites they will perform. The teacher explains that Yawm al-Tarwiyah is the 8th, so the day before is the 7th. The imam teaches the methods of going to Mina, praying at Arafat, performing wuquf, and ifadah (which includes staying at Arafat and the farewell tawaf). The commentary supports this with a hadith from Ibn Umar (radiyallahu anhuma) that the Prophet (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) would deliver such a sermon before Yawm al-Tarwiyah, informing the people of their rituals. Thus, this sermon is a recommended sunnah based on the Prophet's practice.

Key Terms
خطبة (khutbah): A sermon delivered by the imam to teach the pilgrims the rituals before Yawm al-Tarwiyah.
يوم التروية (Yawm al-Tarwiyah): The 8th of Dhul Hijjah, when pilgrims traditionally prepare water and travel to Mina.
افاضة (ifadah): The departure from Arafat after wuquf, also referring to the obligatory tawaf (tawaf al-ifadah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) On the day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah)

Key Takeaway
The imam's sermon on the 7th of Dhul Hijjah is a confirmed sunnah for teaching Hajj rites, based on the Prophet's practice.

Hajj — Pilgrimage

Actions from Yawm al-Tarwiyah to Arafat
Describing the pilgrim's movement to Mina, then to Arafat, and the imam's combined prayer and khutbahs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the sequence of actions from Yawm al-Tarwiyah through Arafat and state the Hanafi ruling (sunnah muakkadah) for each step.

Core Idea
The Prophet's Hajj sets the sunnah: Mina on the 8th, Arafat on the 9th with combined prayer and khutbah before prayer.

This passage outlines the recommended (sunnah muakkadah) procedure for the pilgrim on the 8th and 9th of Dhul Hijjah. Following the Prophet's example, the pilgrim goes to Mina, stays overnight, then proceeds to Arafat. At Arafat, the imam leads a combined Zuhr-Asr prayer and delivers two instructional khutbahs. Understanding this sequence ensures the pilgrim performs Hajj correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key actions on Yawm al-Tarwiyah
After Fajr prayer in Makkah, the pilgrim goes to Mina and stays there, performing all five prayers (Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, Isha, Fajr).
This is based on the hadith of Jabir.
2
Identify the key actions on Yawm Arafah after Fajr
After Fajr on the 9th, the pilgrim proceeds to Arafat and stays there.
The stay at Arafat is the essential part of Hajj.
3
Identify the imam's actions at Arafat after zawal
After the sun declines, the imam leads Zuhr and Asr together, then delivers two khutbahs before the prayer.
The khutbahs are before the prayer, not after.
4
Determine the legal status of these actions
These actions are sunnah muakkadah (emphasized sunnah) based on the Prophet's practice.
Omitting them does not invalidate Hajj but diminishes reward.
5
Note the purpose of the khutbahs
The khutbahs teach the pilgrims the rulings of the remaining Hajj rites: standing at Arafat, Muzdalifah, stoning, sacrifice, shaving, and tawaf al-ziyarah.
This instruction ensures pilgrims perform the rites correctly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳۷) فاذا صلى الفجر يوم التروية بمكة خرج الى منى واقام بها حتى يصلى الفجر يوم عرفة ثم يتوجه الى عرفات فيقيم بها [۶۴۲] (۳۸) فاذا زالت الشمس من يوم عرفة صلى الامام بالناس الظهر والعصر ثم يبتدى فيخطب خطبتين قبل الصلوة يعلم [۲۴] (۳۷) پس جب آٹھویں ذی الحجہ کو مکہ میں فجر کی نماز پڑھے تو منی کی طرف نکلے اور وہاں ٹھہرے یہاں تک کہ نویں تاریخ کو فجر کی نماز پڑھے پھر عرفات کی طرف متوجہ ہو اور وہاں ٹھہرے۔ ذی الحجہ کی آٹھویں تاریخ کو مکہ مکرمہ میں فجر کی نماز پڑھ کر منی کی طرف روانہ ہو جائے اور وہاں ظہر، عصر، مغرب، عشاء اور فجر کی نماز پڑھے۔ اور اس درمیان تکبیر تہلیل اور تلبیہ پڑھتار ہے۔ اور نویں تاریخ کو فجر کی نماز پڑھ کر منی سے عرفات کے لئے روانہ ہو جائے اور عرفات میں جا کر ظہر اور عصر کی نماز اکٹھی پڑھے۔ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کے حج کی جو بی حدیث مسلم شریف اور ابو داؤد شریف میں ہے اس میں اس کی تفصیل ہے۔ دخـلـنـا على جابر بن عبد الله فسال عن القوم حتى انتهى الى ... فلما كان يوما التروية توجهوا الى منى فـ فاهلوا بالحج وركب رسول الله فصلى بها الظهر والعصر والمغرب والعشاء والفجر ثم مكث قليلا حتى طلعت الشمس وامر بقبة من شعر تضرب له بنمرة فسار رسول الله ولا تشك قريش الا انه واقف عند المشعر الحرام كما كانت قريش تصنع في الجاهلية فاجاز رسول الله حتى اتى عرفة فوجد القبة قد ضربت له بنمرة فنزل بها (الف) (مسلم شریف، باب حجتہ النبی ص ۳۹۶ نمبر ۱۲۱۸ را بو داؤد شریف ، باب صفته حجتہ النبی ص ۲۷۰ نمبر ۱۹۰۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ آٹھویں ذی الحجہ کومنی آئے اور وہاں پانچ نمازیں پڑھے اور نویں ذی الحجہ کو فجر کی نماز کے بعد عرفہ آ جائے۔ [۶۴۲) (۳۸) پس جب کہ نویں تاریخ کو سورج ڈھل جائے تو امام لوگوں کو نماز پڑھائے ظہر اور عصر کی ۔ پس نماز سے پہلے دو خطبے لوگوں کو دیں۔ ان دونوں میں نماز ، وقوف عرفہ، وقوف مزدلفہ، رمی جمار نجر، حلق اور طواف زیارت کے احکام سکھلائے۔ سورج ڈھل جانے کے بعد پہلے دو خطبے دے جن میں وقوف عرفہ کے احکام، مزدلفہ میں ٹھہرنے کے احکام، رمی جمار کے احکام ، قربانی کیسے کریں گے اس کے احکام ، حلق کیسے کریں گے اس کے احکام اور طواف زیارت کے احکام کو تفصیل سے بیان کرے۔ اور حاجیوں کو سمجھائے ۔ کیوں کہ اس کی ضرورت ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے دخلنا عن جابر بن عبد الله سأل عن القوم حتى انتهى الى ... حتى اذا زاغت الشمس امر حاشیہ : (الف) پس جب ترویہ کا دن ہوا ( یعنی ذی الحجہ کی آٹھویں تاریخ) تو لوگ منی کی طرف متوجہ ہوئے اور حج کا احرام باندھا اور حضور سوار ہوئے ، پس منی میں ظہر، عصر، مغرب، عشاء اور فجر کی نماز پڑی، پھر تھوڑی دیر ٹھہرے یہاں تک کہ سورج طلوع ہو گیا اور بال کے خیمے کے بارے میں حکم دیا کہ اس کو مقام نمرہ میں عرفات میں نمرہ ایک جگہ ہے ) لگایا جائے۔ پس حضور چلے، قریش کو یقین تھا کہ وہ مشعر حرام مزدلفہ میں ٹھہریں گے۔ جیسا کہ قریش زمانہ جاہلیت میں کیا کرتے تھے۔ لیکن حضور آگے بڑھ گئے یہاں تک کہ عرفات آگئے تو خیمہ کو پایا کہ مقام نمرہ میں لگایا گیا ہے۔ تو آپ وہاں اترے۔
(37) When he prays Fajr on Yawm al-Tarwiyah in Makkah, he goes out to Mina and stays there until he prays Fajr on Yawm Arafah, then he heads to Arafat and stays there. (38) When the sun declines on Yawm Arafah, the imam leads the people in Zuhr and Asr prayers, then begins and delivers two khutbahs before the prayer, teaching [the rites].
Source pages p. 403

Commentary
This passage provides a step-by-step procedure for the pilgrim from the 8th to the 9th of Dhul Hijjah. On the 8th (Yawm al-Tarwiyah), after Fajr prayer in Makkah, the pilgrim goes to Mina and stays there, performing all five prayers (Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, Isha, Fajr) there. Then, after Fajr on the 9th (Yawm Arafah), he proceeds to Arafat. At Arafat, after the sun declines (zawal), the imam leads the combined Zuhr and Asr prayers (prayed together at Zuhr time), and before the prayer he delivers two khutbahs (sermons) teaching the rites of Arafat, Muzdalifah, stoning, sacrifice, shaving, and tawaf al-ziyarah. This practice is based on the Prophet's (sallallahu alayhi wa sallam) Hajj as narrated by Jabir ibn Abdillah (radiyallahu anhuma). The commentary emphasizes the importance of these instructions so that pilgrims perform the rituals correctly.

Key Terms
يوم التروية (Yawm al-Tarwiyah): The 8th of Dhul Hijjah, when pilgrims go to Mina and prepare for Hajj.
يوم عرفة (Yawm Arafah): The 9th of Dhul Hijjah, the most important day of Hajj, spent at Arafat.
افاضة (ifadah): In this context, teaching about tawaf al-ifadah (the obligatory tawaf after returning from Arafat).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Go directly to Arafat
B) Go to Mina and stay until Fajr on Yawm Arafah
C) Perform Tawaf al-Qudum
D) Return to Makkah

Key Takeaway
The actions from Yawm al-Tarwiyah to Arafat are sunnah muakkadah based on the Prophet's practice, emphasizing the sequence of Mina stay and Arafat combined prayer with khutbahs.

The Sermon on the Day of Arafah: Before or After Prayer?
Rulings and proofs for the day of Tarwiyah and Arafat including sermon timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the timing of the two sermons on the day of Arafah, identify the primary proof (hadith of Jabir), and evaluate the Maliki counter-argument.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school holds the Arafah sermon precedes the prayer, based on the explicit sequence in the hadith of Jabir.

The day of Arafah is the pinnacle of Hajj. When the sun declines, the Imam leads the combined Zuhr and Asr prayer and delivers two sermons. But should the sermons come before or after the prayer? The Hanafi and Maliki schools differ. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling, its proof from the Prophet's (ﷺ) practice, and the Maliki objection, clarifying the practical consequence for pilgrims.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify exactly what the Hanafi school rules regarding the timing of the two sermons on the day of Arafah. The matn says: 'then he begins by delivering two sermons before the prayer.' That is the relied-upon position.
The sermon is classified as sunnah muakkadah, not wajib.
2
Identify the opposing school and its view
Imam Malik holds that the sermon should be given after the prayer, analogous to the Eid prayer. Understand the basis for this difference.
The Maliki view relies on a different hadith.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi school cites the detailed hadith of Jabir (Sahih Muslim, Abu Dawud) which explicitly describes the Prophet giving a sermon before leading the combined prayer. Read the relevant portion of the hadith and note the sequence.
The hadith is ahad, so it yields zanni thubut and dalala.
4
Analyse the Maliki proof and Hanafi response
The Maliki school uses a hadith from Ibn Umar that mentions the Prophet combined the prayers 'then addressed the people, then went'. The Hanafi response prioritises the more detailed Jabir narration over the general Ibn Umar report.
The Hanafi response relies on the principle of preferring the more explicit (asrah) over the ambiguous.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The difference is not merely theoretical; it changes the order of rituals for pilgrims on Arafah. Under Hanafi practice, pilgrims listen to the sermon first, then pray. Under Maliki practice, they pray first, then listen.
This reflects a broader madhhab principle about the reliance on detailed sunnah versus general reports.

(37) When he prays Fajr on the day of Tarwiyah in Makkah, he goes out to Mina and stays there until he prays Fajr on the day of Arafah, then he proceeds to Arafat and stays there. (38) When the sun declines on the day of Arafah, the Imam leads the people in Zuhr and Asr, then he begins by delivering two sermons before the prayer, teaching them. Commentary: After praying Fajr on the 8th of Dhul Hijjah in Makkah, he proceeds to Mina and stays there, praying Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, Isha, and Fajr, and reciting takbir, tahlil, and talbiyah. On the 9th, after Fajr, he leaves Mina for Arafat and prays Zuhr and Asr together there. The hadith from Sahih Muslim and Sunan Abi Dawud gives details: We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... until the day of Tarwiyah, they went to Mina and entered ihram for Hajj, and the Messenger of Allah rode and prayed there Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, Isha, and Fajr, then waited a little until sunrise, and ordered a hair tent to be pitched for him at Namirah. The Messenger of Allah proceeded, and the Quraysh thought he would stop at al-Mash'ar al-Haram as they used to do in Jahiliyyah, but he passed until he came to Arafat and found the tent pitched, so he dismounted. From this hadith it is understood that he came to Mina on the 8th and prayed five prayers, and on the 9th after Fajr he came to Arafat. (38) When the sun declines on the 9th, the Imam leads the people in Zuhr and Asr, and before the prayer he gives two sermons teaching the rulings of prayer, standing at Arafat, standing at Muzdalifah, stoning the jamarat, sacrifice, shaving, and Tawaf al-Ziyarah. After the sun declines, he gives two sermons explaining these rulings in detail. There is need for this. The hadith says: We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... until when the sun declined, he commanded... Footnote (a): When the day of Tarwiyah came, the people went to Mina and entered ihram, and the Prophet rode, prayed the five prayers in Mina, then waited until sunrise, ordered a hair tent to be pitched for him at Namirah (a place in Arafat). He proceeded, Quraysh thought he would stop at Muzdalifah, but he went on to Arafat and found the tent pitched, so he dismounted. Then the text of the matn: [The Imam] teaches them the prayer, standing at Arafat and Muzdalifah, stoning the jamarat, sacrifice, shaving, and Tawaf al-Ziyarah. (39) He leads them in Zuhr and Asr at the time of Zuhr with one adhan and two iqamahs. (40) Whoever prays Zuhr in his camel saddle alone prays each of them in its own time according to Abu Hanifah... with the Qaswa camel, and he came to the bottom of the valley and addressed the people saying, 'Your blood and your wealth are sacred to you' etc. (Muslim, Abu Dawud). From this hadith it is understood that he gave the sermon before prayer and taught the rulings of Hajj in detail. According to Imam Malik, the sermon is given after the prayer. Their evidence is the hadith from Ibn Umar: ... until when it was time for Zuhr, the Messenger of Allah went out early, combined Zuhr and Asr, then addressed the people, then went and stopped. (Abu Dawud) This mentions the sermon after prayer, so he gives the sermon after prayer like the Eid prayer.
Source pages p. 404

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and an inter-madhhab dispute. The author first states the ruling for the day of Tarwiyah (8th Dhul Hijjah): after Fajr in Makkah, the pilgrim goes to Mina, stays there until Fajr on the day of Arafah (9th), then proceeds to Arafat. On the day of Arafah, when the sun declines (zawal), the Imam leads Zuhr and Asr together and delivers two sermons before the prayer, teaching the rites. The commentary provides the detailed practice: five prayers in Mina, then departure to Arafat after Fajr on the 9th. The proof is the lengthy hadith of Jabir from Sahih Muslim and Sunan Abi Dawud, which describes the Prophet's actions. The commentary also explains that the sermons cover the rulings of standing at Arafat, Muzdalifah, stoning, sacrifice, shaving, and Tawaf. The author then notes a dispute: Imam Malik holds that the sermon is after the prayer, like Eid, citing a hadith from Ibn Umar. However, the Hanafi position of sermon before prayer is supported by the hadith of Jabir which clearly shows the Prophet gave the sermon before praying. This practical difference affects the sequence of the day's rituals.

Key Terms
يوم التروية (Yawm al-Tarwiyah): The 8th day of Dhul Hijjah when pilgrims proceed to Mina.
عرفة (Arafah): The 9th day of Dhul Hijjah when pilgrims stand at the plain of Arafat; also the name of the place.
خطبتين (khutbatayn): Two sermons delivered by the Imam on the day of Arafah before the Zuhr and Asr prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the two sermons on the day of Arafah are delivered before the combined Zuhr and Asr prayer, a ruling derived from the explicit sequence in the hadith of Jabir.

Combining Zuhr and Asr on Arafah: Conditions and Proof
Ruling on combining two prayers on Arafah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi conditions for combining Zuhr and Asr on Arafah and explain how the hadith of Jabir proves the manner of combination.

Core Idea
Combining Zuhr and Asr on Arafah is a confirmed sunnah restricted to congregation at Arafah in ihram.

On the day of Arafah during Hajj, the Imam leads a special combined prayer at the time of Zuhr. This lesson unpacks the three conditions required for this exception to the normal prayer schedule, and traces the proof from the Prophet's practice. Understanding these conditions ensures the ruling is applied correctly and not confused with general permission for travel.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its exceptions
The matn states that on Arafah, the Imam prays Zuhr and Asr together at Zuhr time with one adhan and two iqamahs. This is an exception to the rule of praying each prayer in its own time. Note that this applies only to the Imam leading a congregation.
The commentary adds three conditions for the combination.
2
List the three conditions
From the commentary: (1) being in the field of Arafah, (2) praying behind the Imam, and (3) being in the state of ihram. If any condition is missing, each prayer is offered in its own time.
These are specific to Hanafi fiqh.
3
Examine the proof from hadith
The hadith of Jabir (Sahih Muslim, Abu Dawud) is cited. It describes the Prophet's action: one adhan, iqamah for Zuhr, then iqamah for Asr with no optional prayer in between. This is the textual basis.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but sufficient for a sunnah ruling.
4
Understand the rationale and exception to qiyas
Combining is contrary to the general analogy (qiyas) that each prayer has a fixed time. The exception is justified by the prophetic practice and the need to hasten to the standing at Arafah.
No sunnah is prayed between the two farz prayers.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi variant for individuals
The lesson includes matn (40): a person praying alone in his camel saddle prays each prayer in its own time according to Abu Hanifa. This implies that the combination is only for congregation, not for an individual.
The Sahibayn may have a different view? The commentary does not mention them, but the statement 'according to Abu Hanifah' indicates an ikhtilaf within the school.

(39) He leads them in Zuhr and Asr at the time of Zuhr with one adhan and two iqamahs. (40) Whoever prays Zuhr in his camel saddle alone prays each of them in its own time according to Abu Hanifah. Commentary: (39) He leads the people in Zuhr and Asr at the time of Zuhr with one adhan and two iqamahs. According to the Hanafis, there are three conditions for combining the prayers: (1) being in the field of Arafah, (2) praying with the Imam, (3) being in ihram. Then Zuhr and Asr can be combined. Otherwise, each prayer is prayed in its own time, because combining is established in hadith contrary to analogy. The hadith says: We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... then he gave the adhan, then iqamah, and prayed Zuhr; then he gave iqamah, and prayed Asr; he did not pray anything between them. Then the Messenger of Allah rode until he came to the standing place. (Muslim, Abu Dawud). From this it is understood that Zuhr and Asr are prayed together. And from the first hadith it is understood that he came immediately after zawal for Zuhr, so Asr is prayed at the time of Zuhr. It is also understood that there is one adhan and two iqamahs, one for Zuhr and one for Asr, and no sunnah prayer is prayed between them, because one hastens to the standing at Arafah.
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. The matn states that on the day of Arafah, the Imam leads the people in Zuhr and Asr combined at the time of Zuhr, using one adhan (the call to prayer) and two iqamahs (the second call). The commentary explains that three conditions are necessary for this combination: being in the field of Arafah, praying behind the Imam, and being in the state of ihram. If any of these conditions is missing, each prayer is performed at its own time. The author notes that combining prayers is an exception to the general rule (qi'yas) and is established by the hadith of Jabir. The hadith explicitly states that the Prophet gave one adhan, then iqamah for Zuhr, then after Zuhr he gave iqamah for Asr without any optional prayer in between. The wisdom is to hasten to the standing at Arafat. This ruling is specific to the Hanafi school; other schools may have different conditions.

Key Terms
جمع بين الصلوة (jam' bayn al-salatayn): Combining two prayers (Zuhr and Asr) at the earlier time on the day of Arafah.
اذان (adhan): The call to prayer, given once for the combined prayers.
اقامتین (iqamatayn): Two iqamahs, one for each prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Two adhans and two iqamahs
B) One adhan and one iqamah
C) One adhan and two iqamahs
D) No adhan, only iqamah

Key Takeaway
Combining Zuhr and Asr on Arafah is a sunnah restricted to three conditions: being at Arafah, praying behind the Imam, and being in ihram.

The Solitary Pilgrim's Combining: Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on solitary prayer combination

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on whether a munfarid (solitary pilgrim) may combine Zuhr and Asr on Arafah, and explain the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence).

Core Idea
For Abu Hanifa, combination requires congregation; the Sahibayn allow it even alone.

The day of Arafah is unique: the sunnah of the Prophet ﷺ was to combine Zuhr and Asr. But what if a pilgrim prays alone, not behind the Imam? This lesson explores a classic intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad. Understanding their proofs and the practical outcome clarifies the school's flexibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disagreement
The passage addresses a specific scenario: a pilgrim who prays Zuhr in his own camel saddle, alone. The dispute is whether he may combine Zuhr and Asr at the time of Zuhr.
The base matn asserts Abu Hanifa's view; the commentary adds the Sahibayn's opposing view.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and reason
Abu Hanifa holds that each prayer must be prayed in its own time. Combining is an exception tied to congregation behind the Imam; the hadith shows the Prophet combined with the people. Without congregation, the exception does not apply.
Abu Hanifa emphasizes the condition of jamā'ah.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and reason
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that even the solitary pilgrim may combine. They argue that the Prophet's action was not conditioned on congregation; the basic permissibility of combining on Arafah is general.
The Sahibayn focus on the general sunnah of combining, not on the specific congregation context.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: a pilgrim who prays alone must pray each prayer separately according to Abu Hanifa, but may combine according to the Sahibayn. This affects ease and time management on Arafah.
The mufta bihi (operative position) is that of the Sahibayn, as it provides ease.
5
Confirm the authoritative tarjih
Later Hanafi scholars (e.g., Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah) prefer the Sahibayn's view for fatwa, because it is more accommodating for pilgrims.
This illustrates how later tarjih can favor the disciples even when they differ from the founder.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[ ٦٤٤] (۴۰) ومن صلى الظهر في رحله وحده صلى كل واحدة منهما في وقتها عند ابي حنيفة [ ٦٤٤] (۴۰) جس نے کجاوے میں تنہا نماز پڑھی تو ہر ایک نماز کو اپنے اپنے وقت میں پڑھے گا امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک اور صاحبین نے فرمایا منفرد بھی دونوں نمازوں کو جمع کرے گا۔ اوپر گزر چکا ہے کہ تین شرطیں ہوں تو میدان عرفات میں جمع بین الصلوتین کرے گا۔ یعنی ظہر اور عصر کو ایک ساتھ ظہر کے وقت میں حاشیہ : (الف) یہاں تک کہ جب سورج ڈھل گیا تو حکم دیا کہ قصواء اونٹنی کو چلایا جائے تو بطن وادی آئے اور لوگوں کو خطبہ دیا ان دما نگم و اموالکم آخر تک ( ب ) ابن عمر سے روایت ہے کہ ... یہاں تک کہ جب ظہر کا وقت ہوا تو حضور اول وقت میں نکلے اور ظہر اور عصر کو جمع کیا پھر لوگوں کو خطبہ دیا پھر چلے اور وقوف عرفہ کیا (ج) پھر اذان دی پھر اقامت کہی اور ظہر کی نماز پڑھی پھر اقامت کہی اور عصر کی نماز پڑھی اور دونوں کے درمیان کوئی نماز نہیں پڑھی ، پھر حضور سوار ہوئے یہاں تک کہ موقف کے پاس آئے۔
(40) Whoever prays Zuhr in his camel saddle alone prays each of them in its own time according to Abu Hanifah. Commentary: (40) He who prays alone in his saddle will pray each prayer in its own time according to Imam Abu Hanifah, and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: Even the solitary person combines both prayers. It has passed above that if three conditions are met, he combines in the field of Arafah, i.e., Zuhr and Asr together at the time of Zuhr. Footnote: (a) Until when the sun declined, he commanded that the Qaswa camel be made to travel, so he came to the bottom of the valley and addressed the people saying, 'Your blood and your wealth are sacred...' (b) From Ibn Umar: ... until when it was time for Zuhr, the Prophet went out early, combined Zuhr and Asr, then addressed the people, then went and performed wuquf at Arafah. (c) Then he gave adhan, then iqamah, prayed Zuhr, then iqamah, prayed Asr, and did not pray anything between them; then the Prophet rode until he came to the standing place.
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute. The matn states: 'Whoever prays Zuhr in his camel saddle alone prays each of them in its own time according to Abu Hanifah.' The commentary clarifies that Imam Abu Hanifah holds that an individual praying alone (i.e., not with the congregation) must pray Zuhr at its time and Asr at its time, and cannot combine them. However, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn) hold that even the solitary person may combine the two prayers if they are at Arafah in ihram. The condition of praying with the Imam is therefore not required according to the Sahibayn. The footnote repeats hadith evidence for combination. The practical difference: a pilgrim who falls behind the congregation or is alone must follow Abu Hanifah's stricter view and pray each prayer separately, or follow the Sahibayn and combine. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that of the Sahibayn, as it is easier and more accommodating.

Key Terms
منفرد (munfarid): A person praying alone, not in congregation with the Imam.
صاحبین (Sahibayn): Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two main students of Abu Hanifah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Yes, but only if they are in ihram
D) No, they cannot even pray Zuhr

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the mufta bihi allows a solitary pilgrim on Arafah to combine Zuhr and Asr, following the view of the Sahibayn over Abu Hanifah for the sake of ease.

Combining Dhuhr and Asr at Arafah: Conditions and Procedure
Ruling on the imam's actions at Arafat including khutbah and combined prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions for combining Dhuhr and Asr at Arafah and explain the Hanafi procedure of one adhan and two iqamahs with khutbah before prayer.

Core Idea
Combining prayers at Arafah is a restricted concession: in Arafah, with the imam, and in ihram.

This lesson examines the specific ruling for the imam on the day of Arafah: leading Dhuhr and Asr together at the time of Dhuhr. The passage outlines the procedure (one adhan, two iqamahs, no sunnah between) and the conditions that make this permissible. It also addresses the inter-madhhab dispute with Imam Malik regarding whether the khutbah comes before or after the combined prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The imam leading the congregation in Dhuhr and Asr together at the time of Dhuhr during Hajj at Arafah. The ruling is that it is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah) for the imam to do so under specific conditions.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith of Jabir ibn Abdullah (RA) describing the Prophet's actions: one adhan, two iqamahs, no sunnah between, and immediate departure to the standing. The source also cites a separate hadith for the khutbah before prayer.
The dalil is ahad but its meaning (dalala) is considered clear (qati) for the Hanafi school.
3
Identify the conditions
From the text, three conditions are extracted: (1) being in the field of Arafah, (2) praying with the imam, and (3) being in ihram. If any condition is missing, each prayer must be performed in its own time.
These conditions restrict the general analogy (qiyas) that prayers must be on time; the concession is an exception.
4
Analyze the ikhtilaf on khutbah timing
The Hanafi school holds the khutbah precedes the combined prayer, based on the explicit sequence in the hadith of Jabir. Imam Malik argues it comes after, similar to Eid khutbahs, citing a hadith from Ibn Umar. The Hanafi response emphasizes the greater authenticity and explicitness of the Jabir hadith.
The practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) is the order of actions on the day of Arafah.
5
Synthesize the procedure
The complete sequence for the imam: deliver the khutbah at the bottom of the valley, then call one adhan for both prayers, make one iqamah for Dhuhr, lead Dhuhr, then make a second iqamah for Asr, lead Asr, and proceed immediately to the standing without any sunnah prayers in between.

(40) And whoever prays Dhuhr in his camel-howdaj alone prays each of them at its own time according to Abu Hanifa. He came on the short-haired she-camel prepared for him until he reached the bottom of the valley, then he addressed the people saying: 'Your blood and your wealth are sacred to you...' etc. (a) (Muslim, Hajjatun Nabiyy, p.397 no.1218 / Abu Dawud, Sifat Hajjatun Nabiyy, p.270 no.1905). From this hadith it is understood that the khutbah is given before the prayer, and he explained the rulings of Hajj in detail.
According to Imam Malik, the khutbah is given after the prayer. His proof is this hadith from Ibn Umar ... until when it was the time of Dhuhr, the Messenger of Allah set out early, combined Dhuhr and Asr, then addressed the people, then set out and stood at Arafah (b) (Abu Dawud, Bab al-Khuruj ila Arafah, p.272 no.1913). It mentions the khutbah after prayer, so the khutbah is given after prayer like the two Eids.
[643] (39) He should lead the people in Dhuhr and Asr prayers at the time of Dhuhr with one adhan and two iqamahs. According to the Hanafi school, if three conditions are met, combining the prayers is permissible: (1) that he is in the field of Arafah, (2) that he prays with the imam, (3) that he is in ihram. Then he can combine Dhuhr and Asr. Otherwise, each prayer is prayed at its own time. Because combining prayers is established in hadith contrary to analogy. (2) In a hadith: 'We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah ... then he called the adhan, then the iqamah, prayed Dhuhr, then the iqamah, prayed Asr, and did not pray anything between them. Then the Messenger of Allah rode until he came to the standing place' (c) (Muslim, Hajjatun Nabiyy, p.397 no.1218 / Abu Dawud, Sifat Hajjatun Nabiyy, p.270/271 no.1905). From this it is understood that Dhuhr and Asr are prayed together. And from the first hadith it is understood that he came immediately after zawal for Dhuhr prayer, which indicates that Asr is prayed at the time of Dhuhr. It is also understood that there is one adhan and two iqamahs: one for Dhuhr and one for Asr. And no sunnah prayer is offered between them, because one is in haste to proceed to the standing at Arafah.
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This is a ruling from the matn of Al-Hidayah about the imam's actions on the day of Arafah. The passage first states the ruling: the imam leads Dhuhr and Asr together at the time of Dhuhr using one adhan and two iqamahs. The commentator then expands this by discussing three aspects: (1) the khutbah before prayer, (2) the conditions for combining, and (3) the specific procedure of adhan and iqamah. The khutbah timing is debated: the Hanafi position, based on the hadith of the Prophet's Hajj, is that the khutbah precedes the prayer, whereas Imam Malik holds that it follows the prayer, analogous to Eid khutbahs. The commentator refutes Malik by noting the explicit sequence in the authentic hadith. The three conditions for combining are: being in the field of Arafah, praying with the imam, and being in ihram. These restrict the permission to combine, which is an exception to the general rule that prayers must be performed at their appointed times. The procedure is one adhan for both prayers, then two separate iqamahs, with no sunnah prayers in between, to expedite the standing at Arafah. The proofs cited are hadiths from Muslim and Abu Dawud.

Key Terms
جمع بین الصلاتین (jama' bayna al-salatayn): Combining two obligatory prayers at one time, specifically Dhuhr and Asr at Arafah.
اذان (adhan): The call to prayer; here one adhan for both Dhuhr and Asr.
اقامت (iqamah): The shorter call to commence prayer; here two iqamahs, one for each prayer.

Lone Individual's Prayer at Arafah: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on combining prayers for the lone individual at Arafah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two positions and their proofs in the intra-Hanafi dispute on combining prayers for the lone individual at Arafah and evaluate the tarjih.

Core Idea
The concession to combine at Arafah is limited to those with the imam; the lone individual must pray each at its time (Abu Hanifa).

When performing Hajj at Arafah, the imam leads a combined Dhuhr and Asr prayer. But what about a pilgrim who prays alone? This passage from Al-Sharh al-Samari presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa rules that the lone individual cannot combine and must pray each prayer at its fixed time, while his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (al-Sahibayn), permit combining. Understanding this ikhtilaf hones your ability to apply conditions to legal concessions and to evaluate contradictory proofs within the same school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the two positions
Read the matn and commentary to pinpoint the exact ruling: the munfarid (lone individual) praying in his camel-howdaj. Abu Hanifa says no combining; Sahibayn say yes.
The issue is whether the condition of 'being with the imam' is necessary.
2
Analyze Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa relies on the Qur'anic verse (An-Nisa 4:103) that establishes fixed prayer times. Combining is an exception, and exceptions are strictly limited to their conditions.
He also adds a rational argument: the hardship of reassembly after dispersal applies only to the congregation.
3
Analyze the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn cite the general practice of the Prophet at Arafah (combining) which does not specify being with the imam, and an athar from Ibn Umar that he combined even when he missed the imam.
They argue that the concession is general for all at Arafah.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response (tarjih)
The commentator sides with Abu Hanifa by restricting the general practice to the congregational context. The Prophet's action is interpreted as specific to the imam, and the athar from Ibn Umar is a personal ijtihad.
The principle: 'prayer at fixed times' is the rule; concession needs strong proof.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
A Hanafi following Abu Hanifa will pray Asr at its own time if not with the imam; following the Sahibayn, he may combine. The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's view.
In practice, most Hanafis follow Abu Hanifa.

(40) Whoever prays Dhuhr in his camel-howdaj alone prays each of them at its own time according to Abu Hanifa. He came on the short-haired she-camel... (as before). This hadith shows that the khutbah is given before the prayer... [Then repeated (39) commentary, then:] (40) The one who prayed alone in his camel-howdaj: he will pray each prayer at its own time according to Abu Hanifa, and the Sahibayn said that even the lone individual combines both prayers. It has passed above that if three conditions are met, he combines at Arafah... [Then defenses and Sahibayn's proof.]
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the lone individual who prays at Arafah not with the imam but alone in his camel-howdaj. Abu Hanifa holds that he must pray Dhuhr at its time and Asr later at its own time; he cannot combine. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say he may combine like the congregant. The commentator first restates the general conditions for combining (being with imam, in ihram, at Arafah) emphasizing that combining is an exception to the general rule from the Qur'an ("prayer is prescribed at fixed times"). Abu Hanifa's argument: combining is a concession limited to those with the imam because of the difficulty of reassembling after dispersal; a lone individual does not face that hardship. The Sahibayn argue from the generality of the practice: the Prophet combined at Arafah without specifying congregational joining, and an athar from Ibn Umar shows he combined even when he missed the imam. The commentator does not explicitly state the mufta bihi, but the Hanafi tarjih typically favors Abu Hanifa's restriction.

Key Terms
منفرد (munfarid): A person praying alone, not in congregation with the imam.
صاحبين (sahibayn): The two companions of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The general practice of the Prophet at Arafah
C) The principle of istihsan
D) Qiyas on the congregant

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the concession to combine at Arafah is only for those with the imam; the lone individual must pray each at its fixed time.

The Standing Place at Arafah: All of Arafah Valid Except Batn Arnah
Ruling on the entire plain of Arafah being valid for standing, except Batn Arnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the valid area for wuquf at Arafah and identify Batn Arnah as excluded, citing the hadith proofs.

Core Idea
All of Arafah is a valid standing place, but Batn Arnah is excluded due to past punishment.

When you perform Hajj, the most critical part is the standing (wuquf) at Arafah. But where exactly within Arafah must you stand? The Hanafi ruling clarifies that the entire plain is acceptable, except one specific valley: Batn Arnah. This lesson unpacks the evidence from two hadiths and explains the recommended spot near Jabal ar-Rahmah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Note that wuquf at Arafah is a rukn (pillar) of Hajj. The passage focuses on the place (mauqif) – where it is valid to stand.
The ruling on the place is that all of Arafah is valid.
2
State the general rule
The text explicitly says: 'و عرفات كلها موقف' – all of Arafah is a standing place. This is the default ruling.
This includes all areas within the boundaries of Arafah.
3
Identify the exception
The exception is Batn Arnah, a valley where previous nations were punished. The hadith orders: 'ارتفعوا عن بطن عرنة' – stay away from Batn Arnah.
Standing in Batn Arnah does not count as wuquf.
4
Examine the proofs
Two hadiths are cited: the first from Ali confirms the whole of Arafah is mauqif; the second from Muhammad ibn Munkadir explicitly excludes Batn Arnah and also warns about Muhassir in Muzdalifah.
Both are ahad but strong in meaning.
5
Note the recommendation
It is mustahabb to stand near Jabal ar-Rahmah because the Prophet stood there. This is an excellence, not a requirement.
The best is to be near the mount, but any spot within Arafah suffices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۶۴۵] (۴۱) ثم يتوجه إلى الموقف ويقرب من جبل الرحمة و عرفات كلها موقف. و بطن عرنة ليس بموقف. أشرفي عرفات كلها موقف. و الأفضل أن يقف عند جبل الرحمة لأن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وقف عنده. و لا يقف ببطن عرنة لأنه عذب بها الأمم السابقة.
و الدليل على أن عرفات كلها موقف: حديث علي بن أبي طالب قال: وقف رسول الله بعرفة فقال: هذه عرفة و هذا الموقف، و عرفة كلها موقف، ثم أفاض حين غربت الشمس. (رواه الترمذي)
و الدليل على ترك بطن عرنة: حديث محمد بن منكدر أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: عرفة كلها موقف و ارتفعوا عن بطن عرنة، و المزدلفة كلها موقف و ارتفعوا عن محسر. (رواه البيهقي و ابن ماجه)
و يندب القرب من جبل الرحمة لأنه موقف النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم.
(41) Then he proceeds to the standing place and draws near to Jabal ar-Rahmah, and all of Arafah is a standing place. And Batn Arnah is not a standing place. The best is to stand near Jabal ar-Rahmah because the Prophet stood there. And do not stand at Batn Arnah because it was there that previous nations were punished. The proof that all of Arafah is a standing place: the hadith of Ali ibn Abi Talib who said: the Messenger of Allah stood at Arafah and said: 'This is Arafah, and this is the standing place, and all of Arafah is a standing place.' Then he departed when the sun set. (Reported by Tirmidhi) The proof for avoiding Batn Arnah: the hadith of Muhammad ibn Munkadir that the Prophet said: 'All of Arafah is a standing place, but stay away from Batn Arnah; and all of Muzdalifah is a standing place, but stay away from Muhassir.' (Reported by Bayhaqi and Ibn Majah) It is recommended to be near Jabal ar-Rahmah because it is the standing place of the Prophet.
Source pages p. 406

Commentary
This is a ruling about the place of standing (wuquf) at Arafah, which is a pillar of Hajj. The passage states that the entire plain of Arafah is valid for standing, except Batn Arnah, which is a valley where divine punishment once fell. The best place to stand is near Jabal ar-Rahmah (the Mount of Mercy) because the Prophet chose that spot. Two authentic hadiths are cited: one from Ali ibn Abi Talib confirming the whole area as mauqif, and another from Muhammad ibn Munkadir explicitly instructing to avoid Batn Arnah. The commentator also notes that markers delineate the boundaries of Arafah. The ruling is straightforward: the performer of Hajj must stand within the boundaries of Arafah any time between noon on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah and dawn on the 10th; standing in Batn Arnah does not count as wuquf.

Key Terms
موقف (mauqif): The place of standing at Arafah during Hajj.
بطن عرنة (Bathn Arnah): A valley near Arafah where standing is not permitted because it is not part of Arafah.
جبل الرحمة (Jabal ar-Rahmah): The 'Mount of Mercy' within Arafah where the Prophet stood; it is mustahabb to stand near it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which area is NOT permissible for standing (wuquf) at Arafah?
A) Near Jabal ar-Rahmah
B) The entire plain of Arafah
C) Batn Arnah
D) Anywhere within the marked boundaries of Arafah

Key Takeaway
The entire plain of Arafah is valid for wuquf, but Batn Arnah is excluded; standing near Jabal ar-Rahmah is recommended but not required.

Combining Prayers at Arafat: Dispute Between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on combining at Arafat for the munfarid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on combining Zuhr and Asr at Arafat for the munfarid, explain the ta'lil (rationale) of each, and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa: combine only with imam; Sahibayn: munfarid also combines — rationale vs. general texts.

At Arafat, it is sunnah to combine Zuhr and Asr at the time of Zuhr when praying with the imam. But what if a pilgrim prays alone? This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the concession of combining extends to the munfarid. The disagreement turns on whether the condition of praying with the imam is inherent in the rationale of the concession.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The dispute is about whether a pilgrim who prays alone (munfarid) may combine Zuhr and Asr at Arafat.
The issue is specific to the Hanafi school; Shafi'i and Maliki schools allow combining without this condition.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and his dalil
Abu Hanifa holds that the munfarid does not combine; he prays each prayer on time. His primary proof is the Quranic prescription of fixed times (Surah an-Nisa 4:103), which is only overridden by a strong proof for the congregation due to the difficulty of gathering again.
The concession is thus restricted to those who pray with the imam.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and their dalil
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani hold that the munfarid does combine. They rely on general hadiths that mention combining at Arafat without any condition, and on the practice of Ibn Umar who combined when he missed the imam.
They give priority to the general textual evidence over the ta'lil.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response to the Sahibayn
The commentary explains that the general hadiths are qualified by the underlying rationale (sabab al-rukhsa): the concession is to ease gathering after dispersion. This rationale only applies to the congregation, not to the individual.
Thus Abu Hanifa specifies the general permission by the condition of praying with the imam.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, a munfarid must pray Asr in its own time; under the Sahibayn, he may combine Asr with Zuhr.
The mufta bihi is not explicit in the text, but the commentary emphasizes conditions, leaning towards Abu Hanifa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

پڑھے گا ورنہ نہیں۔
اپنے اپنے وقت پر نماز پڑھنا آیت کی وجہ سے فرض ہے۔ آیت میں ہے ان الصلوة كانت على المومنين كتابا موقوتا (الف) آیت ۰۳ اسورۃ النساء) آیت سے معلوم ہوا کہ ہر نماز اپنے اپنے وقت کے ساتھ متعین ہے اس لئے بغیر مظبوط دلیل کے نماز اپنے وقت سے مقدم و مؤخر نہیں ہوسکتی۔ اور عرفات میں عصر مقدم ہوئی لیکن جن شرائط کے ساتھ مقدم ہوئی ہے انہیں شرائط کے ساتھ مقدم ہوگی ، اگر وہ شرطیں نہ پائی جائیں تو مقدم نہیں ہوگی ۔ اور امام کے ساتھ نماز پڑھنا شر دی تھی اس لئے امام کے ساتھ نماز نہیں پڑھی اور تنہا اپنے کجاوے میں نماز پڑھی تو مقدم نہیں کرے گا بلکہ عصر کی نماز اپنے وقت میں پڑھے گا (۲) امام کے ساتھ نماز پڑھنے میں جمع اس لئے بھی کرے گا کہ عرفات کے میدان میں بکھرنے کے بعد دوبارہ جمع ہونا مشکل ہوگا اس لئے سہولت کے لئے جمع بین الصلوتین کیا۔ اور تنہا نماز پڑھ رہا ہے تو اس سہولت کی ضرورت نہیں ہے اس لئے جمع بین الصلوتین کی ضرورت نہیں۔
مانده صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ حدیث میں عرفات میں جمع بین الصلوتین کا ذکر کثرت سے ہے اور بغیر کسی شرط کے ہے۔ اس لئے جولوگ امام سے الگ نماز پڑھیں گے وہ بھی جمع بین الصلوتین کریں گے۔ انکی دلیل یہ اثر ہے ان ابن عمر كان يجمع بينهما اذا فاته مع الامام يوم عرفة ( سن سبیھقی ، باب الخطبة يوم عرفة والجمع بين الظهر والعصر ) ج خامس ص ، ۱۸۶، نمبر ۹۴۵۶)
Book of Hajj. May Allah have mercy on him. And Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: The one who prays alone combines between them. [645 (41) Then he proceeds... He will pray? otherwise not. Praying each prayer in its own time is obligatory due to the verse. The verse: 'Indeed prayer is upon the believers a prescribed obligation at specific times' (Surah an-Nisa, verse 103). From the verse it is understood that every prayer is specified with its time, so without a strong proof prayer cannot be advanced or delayed from its time. And at Arafat Asr was advanced, but with the conditions with which it was advanced, it will be advanced; if those conditions are not found, it will not be advanced. And praying with the imam was a condition, so if he did not pray with the imam and prayed alone in his saddle, he will not advance it; rather he will pray Asr in its own time. (2) In praying with the imam, he will combine because after dispersing in the plain of Arafat it is difficult to gather again; therefore for ease the combination of the two prayers was made. And if he is praying alone, there is no need for this ease, so there is no need for combining. The remaining Sahibayn say that the hadith mention combining at Arafat abundantly and without any condition. Therefore, those who pray separately from the imam will also combine. Their evidence is this athar: 'Ibn Umar used to combine between them when he missed [praying] with the imam on the day of Arafah' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, Bab al-Khutbah yawma Arafah wa al-jam' bayn al-Zuhr wa al-Asr, vol. 5, p. 186, no. 9456).
Source pages p. 406

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling of combining Zuhr and Asr at Arafat for the pilgrim who prays alone (munfarid) versus the one who prays with the imam. The matn states: 'Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said: The one who prays alone combines between them.' The commentator explains that according to Abu Hanifa, the basic rule is that each prayer must be performed in its own time, based on the Quranic verse that prescribes prayer at fixed times. Advancing Asr to Zuhr time at Arafat is an exception allowed only under specific conditions. One of those conditions is praying with the imam, because the concession is provided for the congregation to facilitate gathering after dispersion. If a person prays alone, this rationale does not apply, so he must pray each prayer on time. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) disagree. They point to the general hadiths that indicate combining at Arafat without any condition of being with the imam. They cite the practice of Ibn Umar, who would combine even when he missed the imam. Thus, according to the Sahibayn, the munfarid also combines. The text does not explicitly state which view is mufta bihi, but the commentary leans towards Abu Hanifa's position by stressing the condition.

Key Terms
المنفرد (al-munfarid): The one who prays alone, i.e., not in congregation with the imam at Arafat.
جمع بین الصلاتین (jam' bayn al-salatayn): Combining two prayers (Zuhr and Asr) at the time of the earlier one at Arafat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what condition must be met for a pilgrim to combine Zuhr and Asr at Arafat?
A) He must be fasting.
B) He must pray with the imam.
C) He must be on foot.
D) He must stand near Jabal al-Rahmah.

Key Takeaway
Combining prayers at Arafat is a concession conditioned on praying with the imam according to Abu Hanifa, while the Sahibayn extend it to the munfarid based on unconditional transmissions.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
beginner
10 min
Wuquf at Arafat: Place, Imam's Actions, and Ghusl
Rulings and recommendations for standing at Arafat: place, imam's posture and dua, and ghusl

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the valid area for wuquf at Arafat, explain the sunnah actions of the imam during wuquf, and identify the recommendation of ghusl before wuquf.

Core Idea
All of Arafat is a standing place; avoid Batin 'Arnah; the imam should stand on his mount and make dua; ghusl before wuquf is recommended.

This passage from Al-Sharh al-Sameri clarifies key aspects of wuquf at Arafat, the central pillar of Hajj. It first establishes that the entire plain of Arafat (excluding Batin 'Arnah) is valid for standing, debunking the misconception that only a specific spot suffices. Then it describes the sunnah conduct of the imam, who should stand on his mount to be visible, make abundant dua, and teach the rites. Finally, it recommends ghusl before wuquf as an act of purification. Understanding these details ensures that pilgrims perform wuquf correctly and maximize its spiritual reward.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary ruling and recommendation
First, determine the hukm for the place of wuquf: is it valid only at a specific point or all of Arafat? Then identify the sunnah actions for the imam and the recommendation of ghusl.
The text explicitly states 'عرفات كلها مواقف' (all of Arafat is a standing place).
2
Locate the supporting hadith
Find the two hadith quoted: from 'Ali and from Muhammad ibn Munkadir. One affirms the general area; the other excludes Batin 'Arnah.
The hadith are from Tirmidhi and Bayhaqi.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah (legal implication)
Explain how each hadith proves the ruling. For example, the statement 'عرفة كلها موقف' is general and indicates permission. The prohibition 'ارتفعوا عن بطن عرنة' excludes a specific area.
4
Differentiate valid vs preferred
Note that while any part of Arafat (except Batin 'Arnah) is valid, standing near Jabal al-Rahmah is afdal, following the Prophet's practice.
The hadith of Jabir describes the Prophet's specific posture.
5
Summarize the imam's sunnah and ghusl
From the hadith and explicit text, state that the imam should stand on a mount, make dua, and teach rites. Ghusl before wuquf is mustahabb for purification.

حاشیہ : (الف) یقیناً نماز مومنین پر فرض ہے وقت متعین کے ساتھ (ب) حضور عرفہ میں ٹھہرے پس فرمایا یہ عرفہ مظہر نے کی جگہ ہے۔ اور عرفہ پورا نظہر نے کی جگہ ہے۔ پھر سورج غروب ہونے کے بعد چلے (ج) آپ نے فرمایا پورا عرفہ مظہر نے کی جگہ ہے۔ البتہ یبطن عرنہ سے دور رہو۔ اور پورا مزدلفہ مظہر نے کی جگہ ہے البتہ مسر سے دور رہو۔
Then he turns towards the standing place and stands near the mountain [Jabal al-Rahmah], and all of Arafat is the place of standing. There are signs around the plain of Arafat. Wherever he stands within it, the Hajj will be performed. It is better to stand near the mountain, because the Prophet (ﷺ) stood near it. And do not stand near Batin 'Arnah because earlier nations were punished there. The entire plain of Arafat is a place of standing; its proof is the hadith: 'Ali ibn Abi Talib said: The Messenger of Allah stood at Arafat and said: This is Arafah, and it is the standing place, and all of Arafah is a standing place. Then he departed when the sun set.' (Tirmidhi) From this hadith it is known that the entire plain of Arafat is a place of standing. The reason not to stand at Batin 'Arnah is the hadith: 'Muhammad ibn Munkadir reported that the Prophet (ﷺ) said: All of Arafah is a standing place, but avoid Batin 'Arnah. And all of Muzdalifah is a standing place, but avoid Muhassir.' (Bayhaqi, Ibn Majah) From this hadith it is known that one should not stand in Batin 'Arnah. The reason for standing near the mountain is the hadith... [Hadith of Jabir about the Prophet's standing]... From this hadith it is known that standing near the mountain is more virtuous. [646] (42) And it is befitting for the imam to stand at Arafat on his mount and make dua and teach the people the rites. [647] (43) And it is recommended to take a bath before wuquf. The reasoning: bathing is an act of purification, so it is recommended to bathe before wuquf.
Source pages p. 406

Commentary
This passage covers three interconnected rulings regarding wuquf at Arafat. First, it establishes that the entire plain of Arafat—except for Batin 'Arnah—is valid for standing. The proof is the hadith of Ali and the hadith from Muhammad ibn Munkadir, which explicitly state that all of Arafat is a standing place and that Batin 'Arnah is to be avoided. The wisdom is that Batin 'Arnah was a place of punishment for past nations. The preferred spot is near Jabal al-Rahmah, following the Prophet's example. Second, it outlines the sunnah actions of the imam: he should stand on his mount so that people can see him and learn the rites, he should make dua (especially as the best dua is the dua of the day of Arafah), and he should teach the people. The hadith of the Prophet's standing on his she-camel Qaswa', facing the qiblah, and remaining until sunset is the basis. Third, it mentions that ghusl before wuquf is mustahabb (recommended) because it is an act of purification and enhances the worship. The hadith about the Prophet's fasting is cited to show that he was on his mount while questioned about fasting, further supporting the imam's posture. The passage also notes that combining prayers at Arafat is to give more time for dua and dhikr at the standing place.

Key Terms
وقوف عرفة (wuquf 'Arafah): The act of being present at Arafat during the specified time (9 Dhu al-Hijjah). It is a rukn of Hajj.
بطن عرنة (Batin 'Arnah): A specific valley within Arafat where it is not allowed to stand. It is excluded from the valid standing area.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The entire plain of Arafat is valid for wuquf except Batin 'Arnah; the imam should stand on a mount and make dua; ghusl before wuquf is recommended.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
8 min
The Imam's Wuquf on a Mount at Arafat
Ruling with evidence for the imam's wuquf on a mount.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling (mustahabb) for the imam to stand on his mount during wuquf at Arafat and identify the hadith evidence that supports it.

Core Idea
The imam's standing on a mount at Arafat is mustahabb, following the Prophet's own practice.

This passage addresses the recommendation for the imam (the leader of the pilgrimage) to stand on his mount during the wuquf at Arafat. While the entire area of Arafat is a valid standing place (except Batn Aranah), the imam is encouraged to be elevated so that the people can see him and follow the rites. The primary evidence comes from the detailed description of the Prophet's farewell pilgrimage, where he stood on his she-camel al-Qaswa' until sunset.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
The act under discussion is the position of the imam during wuquf at Arafat. Specifically, whether he should stand on his mount or on foot.
The passage focuses on the imam, not the common pilgrim.
2
State the ruling
The ruling is that it is mustahabb (recommended) for the imam to stand on his mount. The text uses the phrase 'yambaghi' (it is appropriate) and the Urdu commentary explicitly says 'mustahabb'.
Mustahabb means recommended but not obligatory.
3
Examine the dalil
The primary evidence is the hadith of Jabir ibn Abdullah describing the Prophet's own wuquf: he rode his she-camel al-Qaswa' to the standing place, faced the qibla, and remained until sunset. This is a fi'li (action-based) sunnah.
The hadith is from Muslim (no. 1218) and Abu Dawud (no. 1905).
4
Understand the wisdom
The reason for this recommendation is that the imam being elevated allows the people to see him and thus learn and correctly perform the rites. The Urdu commentary states: 'So that the people can easily see the imam and by seeing him the common people can perform the rites.'
This is a maslahah (benefit) consideration.
5
Confirm with additional evidence
The hadith of Umm al-Fadl (Bukhari no. 1661) confirms that the Prophet was standing on his camel when he drank milk on the day of Arafat. Also, hadiths on the virtue of supplication on this day reinforce the context.
These provide supporting evidence but the core dalil is the action itself.

حاشیہ : (الف) آپ سوار ہوئے یہاں تک کہ موقف پر آئے اور اپنی قصواء اومنی کا پیٹ چٹان کی طرف کیا اور جبل المشاۃ [؟] کو سامنے رکھا اور قبلہ کا استقبال کیا اور سورج غروب ہونے تک ٹھہرے۔ اور تھوڑی زردی چلی گئی یہاں تک کہ تکیہ غائب ہو گئی (ب) ام الفضل سے روایت ہے کہ ان کے پاس یوم عرفہ میں حضور کے روزے کے بارے میں اختلاف کیا۔ تو بعض نے کہا کہ آپ روزہ دار ہیں اور بعض نے کہا کہ آپ روزہ دار نہیں ہے۔ پس آپ کے پاس دودھ کا پیالہ بھیجا اور آپ اونٹنی پر سوار تھے۔ اور آپ نے دودھ نوش فرمایا (ج) آپ نے فرمایا بہترین دعا عرفہ کے دن کی دعا ہے (1) حضرت ابن عباس فرماتے ہیں کہ حضور کو عرفہ میں دعا کرتے ہوئے دیکھا۔ آپ کے ہاتھ سینے تک تھے جیسے کوئی مسکین مانگ رہا ہو۔
To the standing place, so he stands near the mountain, and all of Arafat is a standing place except the interior of Aranah. (42) And it is appropriate for the imam to stand at Arafat on his mount, and to supplicate, and to teach the people the rites. (43) And it is recommended... We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... then the Messenger of Allah rode until he came to the standing place, and he placed the belly of his she-camel al-Qaswa' towards the rocks, and he placed Jabal al-Masha in front of him, and he faced the qibla, and he remained standing until the sun set and the yellowness left a little until the disk disappeared. (Muslim, no. 1218; Abu Dawud, no. 1905) From this hadith it is known that standing near Jabal ar-Rahmah is more virtuous. (42) And it is appropriate for the imam to stand at Arafat on his mount and to supplicate and to teach the people the rites. It is appropriate for the imam to stand on his mount so that the people can easily see the imam and by seeing him the common people can perform the rites. (2) The Prophet performed wuquf at Arafat riding his she-camel al-Qaswa'. Therefore it is mustahabb for the imam to stand on his mount, while the common people remain below. From Umm al-Fadl bint al-Harith that people disputed before her on the day of Arafat concerning the fast of the Prophet; some said he was fasting, others said he was not. So she sent him a cup of milk while he was standing on his camel, and he drank. (Bukhari, no. 1661) From the above hadith of Muslim no. 1218 it is also known that he was riding al-Qaswa'. From this hadith it is known that the Prophet performed wuquf at Arafat while riding, and he continued to supplicate. Because in a hadith: from Amr ibn Shu'ayb from his father from his grandfather that the Prophet said: The best supplication is the supplication of the day of Arafat. (Tirmidhi, no. 3585) And in another hadith: from Ibn Abbas: I saw the Messenger of Allah supplicating at Arafat with his hands to his chest like a poor person begging. (Bayhaqi, no. 9497) From these hadiths it is known that one should be occupied with supplication in the field of Arafat. Also, combining the two prayers is done so that one may quickly go to the standing place and make supplication and glorification. Footnote: (a) He rode until he came to the standing place, and he placed the belly of his she-camel al-Qaswa' towards the rocks, and placed Jabal al-Masha in front of him, and faced the qibla, and remained standing until the sun set and the yellowness left until the disk disappeared. (b) From Umm al-Fadl: people disputed before her on the day of Arafat about the Prophet's fast; some said he was fasting, others said he was not. So she sent him a cup of milk while he was standing on his camel, and he drank. (c) He said: The best supplication is the supplication of the day of Arafat. (1) Ibn Abbas said: I saw the Prophet supplicating at Arafat with his hands to his chest like a poor person begging.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the imam's wuquf at Arafat. The text first states that all of Arafat is a valid standing place except the interior of Aranah. Then it rules that the imam should stand on his mount, supplicate, and teach the people. The proof comes from the hadith of Jabir describing the Prophet's own wuquf: he stood on his she-camel al-Qaswa' facing the qibla until sunset. The Urdu commentary explains that this is mustahabb so the people can see and follow the imam. Additional evidence is the hadith of Umm al-Fadl confirming the Prophet was riding. Further hadiths emphasize supplication. The hashiyah clarifies the details of the Prophet's wuquf.

Key Terms
الموقف (al-mawqif): The standing place at Arafat where pilgrims halt for wuquf.
الراحلة (al-rahilah): A mount, typically a camel, used for travel.
مناسك (manasik): The rites and ceremonies of Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The imam's standing on a mount at Arafat is mustahabb, based on the Prophet's practice, to facilitate teaching and visibility for the pilgrims.

Ghusl Before Wuquf at Arafat
Short ruling recommending ghusl before wuquf at Arafat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on ghusl before wuquf at Arafat and explain why it is mustahabb.

Core Idea
Ghusl before wuquf is mustahabb—purification is recommended, not required.

In this brief passage, the author states a simple but significant ruling: performing ghusl before the standing at Arafat is mustahabb. The reasoning is straightforward—ghusl is an act of purification, and being in a state of purity before such a sacred rite is commendable. Let us examine the ruling and its basis.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? What is the hukm level (fard/wajib/sunnah/mustahabb)? The text clearly states ghusl before wuquf and calls it mustahabb.
The ruling is explicitly stated as mustahabb.
2
Locate the proof
The author provides a rational proof: 'Ghusl is a matter of purification.' This serves as the dalil (evidence).
No textual proof is cited; the proof is rational (dalil aqli).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does purification justify mustahabb? Since ghusl is inherently purifying, performing it before a sacred rite enhances one's state of ritual purity, making the act meritorious but not obligatory.
This is a straightforward logical connection.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is no significant disagreement among Hanafis or with other schools; all consider ghusl before wuquf recommended. However, some Shafi'is may label it sunnah rather than mustahabb.
The difference in terminology is minor; the practical effect is the same.
5
Determine the authority weight
This ruling appears in later Hanafi works (fatawa mutakhkhirin). It is relied upon for fatwa today.
Authority weight: fatawa mutakhkhirin.

Source Text

That he should perform ghusl before the standing at Arafat. Reason: Ghusl is a matter of purification, therefore performing ghusl before wuquf at Arafat is mustahabb.
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This is a brief ruling stating the recommendation of ghusl before wuquf at Arafat. The reason given is that ghusl is an act of purification, and it is desirable to be in a state of purity when performing this important rite. The ruling is marked as mustahabb (recommended), not wajib.

Key Terms
الغسل (al-ghusl): Full body ablution for purification.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Performing ghusl before wuquf at Arafat is mustahabb (recommended) based on the principle that purification enhances sacred rites.

Striving in Supplication at Arafat
Ruling recommending vigorous supplication at Arafat.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on supplication at Arafat and cite the hadith evidence for its recommendation.

Core Idea
Supplication at Arafat is a highly recommended sunnah demonstrated by the Prophet with earnest humility.

Arafat is the climax of Hajj, and the Prophet ﷺ devoted much of his time there to supplication. This lesson clarifies the ruling that pilgrims should strive in making du'a, emulating the Prophet's humble posture and earnestness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is supplication (du'a) during the stand at Arafat. The text commands 'he should strive' (yajtahid), indicating recommendation, not obligation.
The ruling level is mustahabb (recommended), not fard or wajib.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Ibn Abbas (Bayhaqi) describing the Prophet raising his hands like a poor beggar, showing the manner and emphasis.
Also supported by the hadith 'the best supplication is the supplication on the day of Arafat' (Tirmidhi).
3
Understand the manner of supplication
The Prophet raised his hands to his chest, similar to a needy person begging. This indicates humility and earnestness.
Hanafis recommend raising hands during du'a at Arafat.
4
Note the practical implication
Pilgrims should dedicate a significant part of their time at Arafat to making du'a, striving in abundance and sincerity.
This includes personal supplications, not just prescribed formulas.

The Urdu commentary refers to the hadith of Ibn Abbas where the Prophet raised his hands like a beggar, indicating earnestness. The recommendation is to make abundant dua, as it is the best day for supplication.
