Departure from Arafat After Sunset
Ruling on departure from Arafat to Muzdalifah after sunset

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended time and manner of departure from Arafat and explain the evidence from the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
Depart from Arafat only after sunset, and do so with calmness, not haste.

The ifadah from Arafat to Muzdalifah is a key moment of Hajj. This passage clarifies when and how it should be done according to the Hanafi school: after sunset and with tranquility. The proof is the Prophet's own practice, recorded in a hadith that describes his careful, unhurried departure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the departure (ifadah) from Arafat to Muzdalifah. The ruling in the Hanafi school is mustahabb (recommended).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Jabir ibn Abdullah as narrated in Muslim and Abu Dawud, describing the Prophet's departure after sunset.
The hadith is ahad but muttasil, and its chain is sound.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's action of waiting until sunset and then departing calmly, while saying 'as-sakinah', shows that this is the recommended way. In Hanafi usul, a fi'l (action) of the Prophet without an explicit command of obligation indicates istihbab (recommendation).
No al-amr yufid al-wujub here because the words are a gentle instruction.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is no major ikhtilaf among madhahib on this point; all agree on the time and calm manner, though some may emphasize different aspects.
The Hanafi position is clear and relied upon.
5
Derive the practical ruling
The imam and pilgrims must wait until sunset, then proceed calmly. The imam should go first, and rushing is avoided.
Departing before sunset is not invalid but omits the mustahabb.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فاذا غربت الشمس افاض الأمام والناس معه على هيئتهم حتى يأتو المزدلفة فينزلون بها [۶۵۰]
(۴۶) والمستحب ان ينزلوا بقرب الجبل الذى عليه الميقدة يقال له قزح ۱۳۸ (۴۴) اور دعا میں خوب کوشش کرے۔ اوپر کی حدیث میں گزرا کہ حضور اس طرح دعا کرتے اور ہاتھ اٹھاتے جیسے مانگنے والے مسکین ہوں، اس لئے عرفہ میں خوب دعا کریں۔ [۲۴۹] (۴۵) پس جب سورج غروب ہو جائے تو امام عرفہ سے چلے اور لوگ بھی ان کے ساتھ چلے اپنی ہیئت پر یہاں تک کہ مزدلفہ آئے اور وہاں اترے۔
میدان عرفات میں شام تک رہے اور غروب آفتاب کے بعد وہاں سے چلے۔ پہلے امام چلے پھر عوام اس کے ساتھ چلے اور دوڑے نہیں۔ بلکہ اپنی ہیئت پر چلے۔
قال دخلنا على جابر بن عبد الله ... فلم يزل واقفا حتى غربت الشمس وذهبت الصفرة قليلا حتى غاب القرص واردف اسامة خلفه ودفع رسول الله وقد شنق للقصواء الزمام حتى ان رأسها ليصيب مورك رحله ويقول بيده اليمنى ايها الناس السكينة السكينة كلما اتى جبلا من الحبال ارخى لها قليلا حتى تصعد حتى اتى المزدلفة (الف) (مسلم شریف، باب حجتہ النبی ص ۳۹۸ نمبر ۱/۱۲۱۸ ابوداؤد شریف، باب صفته حجتہ النبی ص ۲۷۱ نمبر ۱۹۰۵ و باب الدفعه من عرفۃ ص ۲۷۲ نمبر ۱۹۲۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مغرب کے بعد عرفہ سے چلے اور یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ اطمینان سے چلے تیزی نہ کرے۔
When the sun has set, the imam and the people with him depart in their state until they come to Muzdalifah and alight there. (46) And it is mustahabb that they alight near the mountain upon which is the lighthouse, called Quzah. (44) And he should strive in supplication. In the hadith above it passed that the Prophet used to supplicate and raise his hands like a poor person begging, therefore in Arafat one should supplicate much. (45) After the sun has set, the imam moves from Arafat and the people with him move in their state until they come to Muzdalifah and alight there. They remain in the field of Arafat until evening, and after sunset they move from there. The imam moves first, then the common people move with him, and they do not run but move in their state. He said: We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... and he continued standing until the sun set and the yellowness left a little until the disk disappeared, and he seated Usama behind him, and the Messenger of Allah departed, and he tightened the halter of al-Qaswa' until its head touched the front of the saddle, and he said with his right hand: 'O people, calmness, calmness!' Whenever he came to a hill from the ropes, he slackened it a little until it ascended, until he came to Muzdalifah. (Muslim, no. 1218; Abu Dawud, no. 1905, 1922) From this hadith it is known that he departed from Arafat after Maghrib, and it is also known that he proceeded calmly, not quickly.
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling for the departure (ifadah) from Arafat to Muzdalifah. The imam and all pilgrims proceed after sunset, maintaining a calm and composed pace. The proof is the hadith of Jabir describing the Prophet's own departure: he remained until sunset, then moved with Usama behind him, and he repeatedly said 'as-sakinah, as-sakinah' (calmness), and he would ease the camel's reins on hills. This shows the recommended manner: not rushing but moving serenely. The Urdu commentary emphasizes that the imam goes first, then the people, and they do not run.

Key Terms
الإفاضة (al-ifadah): The departure from Arafat to Muzdalifah after sunset.
السكينة (as-sakinah): Calmness, tranquility; the Prophet instructed pilgrims to proceed calmly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's practice shows that departure from Arafat after sunset, with calmness, is the recommended (mustahabb) way.

Alighting in Muzdalifah Near Jabal Quzah
Ruling recommending alighting near Jabal Quzah in Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended place for alighting in Muzdalifah and identify the evidence (dalil) from hadith and Quran.

Core Idea
Alighting near Jabal Quzah in Muzdalifah is mustahabb because the Prophet stayed there.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling on where to stay during the night at Muzdalifah. The passage explains the recommended location near Jabal Quzah, also known as al-Mash'ar al-Haram, and provides the evidence from the Prophet's practice (Sunnah) and the Quran.

Guided Path
1
Identify the recommended act
The act is alighting (نزول) in Muzdalifah, specifically near the mountain called Jabal Quzah.
The mountain has a lighthouse (ميقدة).
2
Determine the hukm level
The text states it is mustahabb (recommended), not wajib. This is based on the Prophet's action, which in Hanafi usul indicates recommendation unless accompanied by a command.
Mustahabb means rewarded but not obligatory.
3
Identify the first proof (Sunnah)
The hadith of Jabir describes the Prophet riding to al-Mash'ar al-Haram, facing qibla, and making supplication until near dawn. This proves the virtue of that specific spot.
The hadith is from Muslim, no. 1219.
4
Identify the second proof (Quran)
The verse 2:198 says 'remember Allah at the Sacred Monument (المشعر الحرام)'. Hanafis identify this as Jabal Quzah, though the entire Muzdalifah is considered the monument.
The verse is a general command; the specific location is derived from practice.
5
Understand the scope
The entire Muzdalifah except Wadi Muhassir is valid for staying, but staying near Jabal Quzah is the best and recommended.
This is from the broader Hanafi fiqh context.

Source Text

(46) It is mustahabb to stay near that mountain upon which is the lighthouse, which is called Quzah. In Muzdalifah, it is mustahabb to stay near Jabal Quzah. Commentary

Departing from Arafat: Sunnah Acts and the Manner of Departure
Ruling on departure from Arafat after sunset with calmness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two sunnah acts before standing at Arafat and explain the Hanafi ruling on departure from Arafat after sunset, including the proof from the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
The Prophet's calm departure after sunset establishes the sunnah; haste contradicts the sunnah.

This passage from Al-Sharh al-Sameri teaches two important sunnah acts of Hajj: performing ghusl before standing at Arafat and exerting in supplication. It then focuses on the moment of departure from Arafat — after sunset — and the manner of that departure, which must be calm and unhurried, as demonstrated by the Prophet himself. The hadith from Jabir provides the primary evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the initial sunnah acts
The passage first mentions two recommended acts: performing ghusl before standing at Arafat and striving in supplication. These are sunnah and enhance the reward of the stay.
These are separate from the departure ruling.
2
Locate the key ruling on departure
The ruling states that when the sun sets, the imam and the people depart from Arafat to Muzdalifah. The timing (after sunset) is part of the recommended manner.
Hanafi considers this sunnah, not wajib.
3
Examine the proof from hadith
The hadith from Jabir describes the Prophet's own departure: he waited until the sun fully set, seated Usamah behind him, calmed his camel, and verbally instructed the people to be calm.
The Prophet's action and command together indicate a recommended manner.
4
Extract the legal point
The key legal takeaway is that calmness (sakinah) during departure is a sunnah. The Prophet's verbal command 'be calm' emphasizes this.
This is the basis for the Hanafi position that rushing is disliked (makruh).
5
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some scholars consider departure after sunset as wajib. The Hanafi school maintains it is sunnah muakkadah, based on the dalil being zanni and the absence of an explicit command for obligation.
The practical consequence: leaving early is makruh tanzihi according to Hanafis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ان يغتسل قبل الوقوف بعرفة (44) ويجتهد فى الدعاء (45) فاذا غربت الشمس افاض الأمام والناس معه على هيئتهم حتى يأتو المزدلفة فينزلون بها. قال دخلنا على جابر بن عبد الله ... فلم يزل واقفا حتى غربت الشمس وذهبت الصفرة قليلا حتى غاب القرص واردف اسامة خلفه ودفع رسول الله وقد شنق للقصواء الزمام حتى ان رأسها ليصيب مورك رحله ويقول بيده اليمنى ايها الناس السكينة السكينة كلما اتى جبلا من الحبال ارخى لها قليلا حتى تصعد حتى اتى المزدلفة
He should perform ghusl before standing at Arafat (44) and exert himself in supplication (45). When the sun sets, the imam and the people with him depart in their state until they come to Muzdalifah and alight there. He said: We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... and he kept standing until the sun set and the yellowness disappeared a little until the disk disappeared, and he seated Usamah behind him, and the Messenger of Allah set out, and he tightened the reins of al-Qaswa until its head touched the front of the saddle, and he said with his right hand: 'O people, be calm, be calm.' Whenever he came to a hill from the ropes, he loosened it a little until it ascended, until he came to Muzdalifah.
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This passage states two recommended acts (sunnah) for the Day of Arafah: performing ghusl before standing at Arafat, and exerting oneself in supplication. It then gives the ruling that after sunset, the imam and all pilgrims must depart from Arafat to Muzdalifah, maintaining a calm and dignified pace. The author supports this with a hadith from Jabir describing the Prophet's own departure: he waited until full sunset, took Usamah behind him, controlled his camel's pace, and repeatedly told the people to be calm. This hadith is the primary proof for the recommended manner of departure (ifadah) from Arafat.

Key Terms
عرفة (Arafat): The plain southeast of Makkah where pilgrims stand on 9th Dhul-Hijjah; the main ritual of Hajj
مزدلفة (Muzdalifah): A place between Arafat and Mina where pilgrims spend the night after Arafat
السكينة (al-sakinah): Calmness and tranquility; not rushing during the departure from Arafat

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) 'Hasten to Muzdalifah'
B) 'O people, be calm, be calm'
C) 'Seek forgiveness'
D) 'Make haste slowly'

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's departure from Arafat after sunset with calmness establishes an emphasized sunnah; pilgrims should follow this example and avoid haste.

Staying Near Jabal Qazh at Muzdalifah
Recommendation to stay near Jabal Qazh (al-Mash'ar al-Haram) in Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the recommended place for staying in Muzdalifah and explain the evidence for its virtue, while distinguishing between the wajib and mustahab elements.

Core Idea
Staying near Jabal Qazh is mustahab; the whole Muzdalifah fulfills the wajib.

This lesson examines the preferred location within Muzdalifah for the night halt during Hajj. While staying anywhere in Muzdalifah is necessary (wajib), the text highlights the virtue of alighting near the mountain called Qazh, identified with al-Mash'ar al-Haram, based on the Prophet's practice and a Quranic verse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action is being discussed (staying/night halt in Muzdalifah) and its legal status (mustahab – recommended).
The text begins with 'wa al-mustahab an yanzilu...' clearly indicating recommendation.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence cited: a Quranic verse (2:198) and a hadith from Jabir describing the Prophet's actions at al-Mash'ar al-Haram.
The verse commands remembrance at al-Mash'ar al-Haram, and the hadith shows the Prophet heading there specifically.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how each proof indicates the virtue of Qazh. The verse identifies the place for dhikr; the hadith shows the Prophet choosing that spot for supplication.
The Prophet's act of facing the qiblah and supplicating there demonstrates its merit.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Compare the Hanafi view (staying in Muzdalifah is wajib; staying near Qazh is sunnah) with views that consider the stay itself as wajib or that specify the exact location as obligatory.
The Hanafi position emphasizes that any part of Muzdalifah fulfills the wajib, but the specific place is recommended.
5
Synthesize the practice
Conclude that pilgrims should aim to stay near the area of Qazh for extra reward, but their stay is valid elsewhere in Muzdalifah. If they miss the wajib stay entirely, a dam is required.
The practical application balances between the recommended and obligatory elements.

Source Text

Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This passage discusses the recommended (mustahab) place to stay in Muzdalifah: near the mountain called Qazh, which had a fire-place (mayqidah) from pre-Islamic times. The author provides two proofs: a Quranic verse (2:198) commanding remembrance at al-Mash'ar al-Haram, which is interpreted as Jabal Qazh, and a hadith from Jabir describing the Prophet's stay at that very place, where he faced the qiblah and made supplication until early morning before departing before sunrise. This establishes the virtue of staying near this mountain.

Key Terms
قزح (Qazh): A mountain in Muzdalifah upon which a fire was lit in pre-Islamic times; identified as al-Mash'ar al-Haram
المشعر الحرام (al-Mash'ar al-Haram): The sacred site in Muzdalifah, specifically Jabal Qazh; the place for dhikr after Arafat
ميقدة (mayqidah): Fire-place; a place where fire is kept for light or signal

Combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah
Ruling on praying Maghrib and Isha combined at Muzdalifah with one adhan and one iqamah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah and identify the prophetic proof (dalil) for using one adhan and one iqamah.

Core Idea
At Muzdalifah, Maghrib and Isha are prayed together at Isha time with a single adhan and single iqamah – a unique Hajj dispensation.

This lesson explains a special sunnah for Hajj pilgrims: combining the Maghrib and Isha prayers at Muzdalifah on the night of the 9th of Dhul Hijjah. The text gives the ruling and supports it with a hadith from Ibn Umar showing the Prophet's practice. Understanding this helps pilgrims follow the sunnah correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prescribed action
Read the first sentence: the imam prays with the people Maghrib and Isha in the time of Isha with one adhan and one iqamah. Note the key elements: combination, time, single calls.
This is the ruling itself.
2
Locate the dalil
The author then cites a hadith from Ibn Umar. Identify the source (Sahih Muslim) and the exact wording. Notice that the hadith confirms the one iqamah.
The dalil is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but sufficient for a sunnah ruling.
3
Analyze the proof's structure
The hadith describes the Prophet's action (fi'l). In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's action indicates recommendation (sunnah) unless proven otherwise. The explicit mention of 'one iqamah' is the key proof.
4
Understand the Hanafi reasoning
Why one iqamah suffices? Because all worshippers are already gathered and Isha is at its proper time. This is a concession (rukhsah) for Hajj, not a general rule.
Some narrations mention two iqamahs, but the Hanafi school prefers the more famous one.
5
Contrast with normal practice
Normally, each fard prayer has its own adhan and iqamah. Here, both are combined into one call each. Recognize that this is a specific dispensation, not a model for travel outside Hajj.
This distinction is important to avoid misunderstanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويصلى الامام بالناس المغرب والعشاء فى وقت العشاء باذان واقامة. حديث: عن ابن عمر قال جمع رسول الله بين المغرب والعشاء بجمع صلى المغرب ثلاثا والعشاء ركعتين باقامة واحدة.
And the imam prays with the people Maghrib and Isha in the time of Isha with one adhan and one iqamah. Hadith: Ibn Umar said: The Messenger of Allah combined Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah; he prayed Maghrib three rak'ahs and Isha two rak'ahs with one iqamah.
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling for the night prayer at Muzdalifah: the imam leads the congregation in combining Maghrib and Isha prayers at the time of Isha (i.e., delaying Maghrib to Isha time). The combination is done with a single adhan and a single iqamah for both prayers. The author supports this with a hadith from Ibn Umar stating the Prophet did exactly that: prayed Maghrib (3 rakah) and Isha (2 rakah) with one iqamah. The commentary adds that since all worshippers are present and Isha is being prayed at its proper time, there is no need for a second iqamah. This is a specific dispensation for the Hajj pilgrims.

Key Terms
جمع (jam'): Combining two prayers at one time; specifically here delaying Maghrib to Isha time at Muzdalifah
اذان (adhan): The call to prayer; here one adhan for both prayers
اقامة (iqamah): The second call immediately before prayer; here one iqamah for both

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Both prayers together at Maghrib time
C) Both prayers together at Isha time with one adhan and one iqamah
D) Only one prayer is prayed at Muzdalifah

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's practice at Muzdalifah was to combine Maghrib and Isha at Isha time with one adhan and one iqamah, which is the sunnah for pilgrims.

Invalidity of Maghrib Prayed on the Way to Muzdalifah
Ruling on praying Maghrib before reaching Muzdalifah on the night of Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying Maghrib before Muzdalifah and identify the intra-madhhab disagreement between Abu Hanifa/Muhammad and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
Maghrib on the night of Muzdalifah must be prayed at Muzdalifah, not on the road.

This lesson examines a specific hajj ruling: the validity of Maghrib prayer if performed while traveling from Arafat to Muzdalifah. The source text presents the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad that such a prayer is invalid, supported by prophetic practice. You will also learn about an intra-Hanafi difference, likely with Abu Yusuf, and the relied-upon position for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Understand that the act is praying Maghrib on the road (fi al-tariq) between Arafat and Muzdalifah. The ruling according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is 'lam yajuz' – not valid, i.e., batil.
The Arabic 'lam yajuz' indicates invalidity requiring repetition.
2
Recognize the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Note that only Abu Hanifa and Muhammad are mentioned; Abu Yusuf is omitted. This suggests he may hold a different view, possibly that the prayer is valid. The mufta bihi is the majority view.
Intra-madhhab differences are common in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Analyze the hadith evidence
Examine the hadith of Usamah: the Prophet delayed Maghrib until reaching Muzdalifah, saying 'al-salatu amamak' (the prayer is ahead of you). This indicates the proper time for Maghrib that night is at Muzdalifah, not earlier.
The hadith is narrated in Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim.
4
Determine the practical consequence
If a pilgrim prays Maghrib on the way, the prayer is batil and must be repeated after arriving at Muzdalifah. If Abu Yusuf's view were taken, no repetition would be needed.
The 'thamarah al-khilaf' is whether repetition is obligatory.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi
The author presents Abu Hanifa and Muhammad's view as the established ruling. Later Hanafi authorities (e.g., al-Hidayah) adopt this as the operative position for fatwa.
Zahir al-riwayah supports this position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن صلى المغرب فى الطريق لم يجز عند ابي حنيفة و محمد رحمهما. حديث: عن اسامة بن زيد انه سمعه يقول دفع رسول الله من عرفة ... فقلت له الصلوة قال الصلوة امامك فجاء المزدلفة فتوضأ فاسبغ ثم اقيمت الصلوة فصلي المغرب.
And whoever prays Maghrib on the way is not valid according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them). Hadith: Usamah ibn Zaid heard him say: The Messenger of Allah set out from Arafat... I said to him, 'The prayer (time).' He said, 'The prayer is ahead of you.' Then he came to Muzdalifah, performed wudu thoroughly, then the iqamah was given, and he prayed Maghrib.
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific situation: a pilgrim who prays Maghrib while still on the road between Arafat and Muzdalifah, before reaching Muzdalifah. According to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad, such a prayer is not valid (la yajuz). The reason is that the time for Maghrib on that night has been shifted to Isha time as a dispensation; thus, praying before reaching Muzdalifah is praying before its proper time. The pilgrimage must repeat it (according to the commentary). The author cites a hadith from Usamah: when he suggested prayer on the way, the Prophet replied 'The prayer is ahead of you,' and then prayed only after reaching Muzdalifah. This shows that the only valid time for Maghrib that night is after arriving. Abu Yusuf may have a different view, but the relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

Key Terms
لم يجز (lam yajuz): Not valid; the prayer is invalid and must be repeated
في الطريق (fi al-tariq): On the road between Arafat and Muzdalifah, before arriving at Muzdalifah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, what is the ruling if a pilgrim prays Maghrib on the way to Muzdalifah?
A) It is valid and no repetition needed
B) It is invalid and must be repeated
C) It is makruh but valid
D) It is valid only if prayed individually

Key Takeaway
Maghrib on the night of Muzdalifah must be performed only after reaching Muzdalifah; praying on the road is batil according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

Combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah
Ruling on the Imam combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for combining Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah and explain the proof from the hadith.

Core Idea
At Muzdalifah, Maghrib and Isha are combined at Isha time with one adhan and one iqamah.

This passage addresses a specific practice during Hajj: how the Imam leads the combined Maghrib and Isha prayers at Muzdalifah. The ruling is based on the Prophet's (peace be upon him) action, which is a confirmed sunnah. Understanding this method is essential for anyone performing Hajj, as it is a unique Sunnah of the farewell pilgrimage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? The Imam combines Maghrib and Isha at the time of Isha with one adhan and one iqamah. The ruling is sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah).
This combination is jam' ta'khir, delaying Maghrib to Isha time.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith from Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) in Sahih Muslim. The Prophet performed the two prayers at Muzdalifah with one iqamah.
The hadith is quoted in the commentary.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? The Prophet's action (fi'l) shows desirability. The phrase 'with one iqamah' indicates that a single iqamah suffices; a second is not required.
Hanafis consider the Prophet's fi'l as evidence for sunnah, not obligation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
There is an alternative narration (Muslim no. 1318) that mentions two iqamahs. Some scholars adopt that view, but the Hanafi school prefers the first hadith as more reliable, or as the basis for mufta bihi.
The intra-Hanafi difference: some early Hanafis allowed two iqamahs, but the relied-upon view is one.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Why is one iqamah preferred? The hadith with one iqamah is clearer and more directly on point. Also, after Maghrib the congregation is already present, so a second call is unnecessary. This is the mufta bihi position.
Tarjih authority: the text itself and the principle of needlessness of repetition.

ان دونوں حدیثوں سے معلوم ہوا کہ جبل قزح کے پاس ٹھہر نا زیادہ بہتر ہے۔
المقيدة : آگ جلنے کی جگہ، زمانہ جاہلیت میں اس پہاڑ کے نزدیک آگ جلانے کی جگہ تھی جس کو مقیدہ کہتے ہیں۔ [۶۵۱] (۴۷) اور امام لوگوں کو نماز پڑھائیں گے مغرب اور عشاء کی عشاء کے وقت میں ایک اذان اور ایک اقامت کے ساتھ ۔ تشریح امام مزدلفہ میں بھی جمع بین الصلوتین کریں گے اور یہ جمع تاخیر کریں گے ۔ اور عشا کے وقت میں مغرب کی نماز پڑھیں گے۔ حدیث میں ہے عن ابن عمر قال جمع رسول الله الله بين المغرب والعشاء بجمع صلى المغرب ثلاثا والعشاء ركعتين باقامة واحدة (ب) ( مسلم شریف ، باب الافاضه من عرفات الى المز دلفته و استحباب صلوتى المغرب والعشاء جميعا بالمزدلفة في هذه الليلة ص ۴۱۷ نمبر ۳۱۱۴/۱۲۸۸) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ ایک اذان اور اقامت سے دونوں نماز پڑھے (۲) چونکہ مغرب کی نماز پرھنے کے بعد تمام نمازی و ہیں موجود ہیں اور نماز عشا اپنے وقت پر پڑھی جارہی ہے اس لئے دوبارہ اقامت کہنے کی ضرورت نہیں۔ اس حدیث سے پر یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ مزدلفہ میں مغرب اور عشا کو جمع کر کے پڑھیں گے۔
و دوسری حدیث میں دو مرتبہ اقامت کہنے کا تذکرہ ہے (مسلم شریف نمبر ۱۳۱۸) حتى انى المزدلفة ، فصلى بها المغرب والعشاء باذان واحد واقامتین (مسلم شریف نمبر ۱۳۱۸)
The Imam prays with the people Maghrib and Isha at the time of Isha with one adhan and one iqamah. ... Explanation: The Imam in Muzdalifah will also combine the two prayers, and this is a delay (jam' ta'khir). He will pray Maghrib at the time of Isha. There is a hadith from Ibn Umar that the Messenger of Allah combined Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah, praying Maghrib three rak'ahs and Isha two rak'ahs with one iqamah. This hadith shows that he prayed both prayers with one adhan and one iqamah. Since after Maghrib all the worshippers are present and Isha is being prayed at its time, there is no need to repeat the iqamah. Another hadith mentions two iqamahs.
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage contains a ruling on the manner of combining Maghrib and Isha prayers at Muzdalifah during Hajj. The Imam performs this combination at the time of Isha with one adhan and one iqamah, following the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him). The commentary explains that this is a delayed combination (jam' ta'khir), moving Maghrib to Isha time. The primary proof is a hadith from Ibn Umar reporting that the Prophet prayed Maghrib (3 rak'ahs) and Isha (2 rak'ahs) with one iqamah. The commentator notes that after Maghrib, the congregation remains present, so a second iqamah is unnecessary. However, another narration mentions two iqamahs, indicating a difference in practice. The Hanafi school adopts the view of one iqamah as the preferred method.

Key Terms
جمع بين الصلوتين (jam' bayn al-salatayn): Combining two prayers in one time, specifically Maghrib and Isha at Muzdalifah in a delayed manner (jam' ta'khir).
اذان واقامة (adhan wa iqamah): The call to prayer (adhan) and the commencement call (iqamah) used for congregational prayer.

Ruling on Praying Maghrib on the Way to Muzdalifah
Intra-Hanafi dispute on Maghrib timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi majority and minority positions on praying Maghrib before Muzdalifah and evaluate the evidence for each.

Core Idea
Praying Maghrib before Muzdalifah: Abu Hanifa & Muhammad rule invalid; Abu Yusuf rules valid but sunnah missed.

During Hajj, the timing of Maghrib prayer on the day of Arafah is unique. The established sunnah is to delay Maghrib until reaching Muzdalifah, but what if a pilgrim prays on the way? This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad consider such a prayer invalid, while Abu Yusuf holds it valid. We'll analyze the evidence and practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
State the majority Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani: praying Maghrib on the way to Muzdalifah is not valid (la yajuz) and must be repeated.
This is the relied-upon position in the school.
2
Identify the minority position
State Abu Yusuf's view: the prayer is valid but the sunnah of praying in Muzdalifah is missed; no repetition needed.
Abu Yusuf considers the time of Maghrib to enter at sunset as usual.
3
Follow the evidence for the majority
Examine the hadith of Usama ibn Zayd and the athar of Ibn Mas'ud, which indicate that the time for Maghrib on that day is shifted to after reaching Muzdalifah.
The Prophet said 'al-salah amamak' (the prayer is ahead of you).
4
Follow the evidence for the minority
Look at the athar of Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr that one may pray where convenient when the time enters.
Abu Yusuf interprets this to mean the time is not shifted.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Understand why the majority position is preferred: stronger dalil and consistent practice of the Prophet.
The mufta bihi is the position of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

[۶۵۲] (۴۸) ومن صلى المغرب فى الطريق لم يجز عند ابي حنيفة و محمد رحمهما

اتاق عرفات سے چل کر مزدلفہ آرہا ہو اور مزدلفہ سے پہلے راستہ میں مغرب کی نماز پڑھ لی تو طرفین کے نزدیک نماز کو دوبارہ لوٹانا ہوگا۔ (1) اس لئے کہ آج کے دن کی مغرب کی نماز کا وقت بدل گیا اور مزدلفہ جانے کے بعد اس کا وقت ہو گا۔ اس لئے وقت سے پہلے نماز پڑھی ہے (۲) حدیث میں ہے اس دن نماز کا وقت حاجیوں کا بدل گیا۔ عن اسامة بن زيد انه سمعه يقول دفع رسول الله من عرفة ... فقلت له الصلوة قال الصلوة امامك فجاء المزدلفة فتوضأ فاسبغ ثم اقيمت الصلوة فصلي المغرب (ج) ( بخاری شریف، باب الجمع بین الصلوة بالمز دلفت ص ۲۷ نمبر ۱۲۷۲ مسلم شریف ، باب استحباب ادامتہ الحاج التلبیہ ص ۲۱۶ نمبر ۱۲۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ نماز کا وقت آگے ہے یعنی مزدلفہ پہنچ کر ہے (۳) ایک اثر میں ہے قال عبد الله بن مسعود هما صلواتان تحولان عن وقتهما صلوة المغرب بعد ما يأتى الناس المزدلفة والفجر حين يبزغ الفجر قال رایت النبي الله يفعله (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب من اذن واقام لکل واحد منهما ص ۲۲۷ نمبر ۱۶۷۵) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ آج کے دن مغرب کی نماز کا وقت ہی بدل گیا ہے اس لئے وقت سے پہلے نماز پڑھے گا تو اس کو لوٹانا ہوگا۔ نا امام ابو یوسف کے نزدیک مزدلفہ کے اندر نماز مغرب پڑھنا سنت ہے۔ اس لئے اگر مزدلفہ کے اندر نماز نہیں پڑھی تو لوٹانے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے ۔ کیونکہ مغرب کی نماز کا وقت ہو گیا ہے۔ اس لئے سنت کے خلاف کیا۔ لیکن نماز ہو گئی۔ نماز لوٹانے کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ ان کی دلیل یہ اثر ہے عن عبد الله بن زبير قال من سنة الحج ... ثم يفيض فيصلى بالمزدلفة او حيث قضى الله عز وجل ثم يقف بجمع (ب) ( سنن میتی ، باب من قال يصليهما بالمز دلفته او حیث قضی اللہ عز و جل ج خامس ص ۱۹۹، نمبر ۲ ۹۵۰) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ جہاں موقع ملے اور مغرب کا وقت ہو جائے تو نماز پڑھ سکتا ہے۔
And whoever prays Maghrib on the way, it is not allowed according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. ... Explanation: One who departs from Arafat and heads to Muzdalifah, and prays Maghrib before reaching Muzdalifah on the way, then according to both (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) the prayer must be repeated. Because the time for Maghrib on this day has changed, and its time becomes after reaching Muzdalifah. Therefore, the prayer was performed before its time. There is a hadith that the prayer time on that day is changed for the pilgrims. ... According to Imam Abu Yusuf, praying Maghrib within Muzdalifah is sunnah; if one does not pray there, there is no need to repeat because the time for Maghrib had already come, so he only acted against the sunnah, but the prayer is valid. His evidence is an athar that one can pray where convenient when the time enters.
Source pages p. 409

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of Maghrib prayer if performed on the way to Muzdalifah before reaching the plain. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani rule that such a prayer is invalid (la yajuz) and must be repeated (dubaarah lautana). Their reasoning is that the time for Maghrib on the Day of Arafat is shifted: it does not enter until after reaching Muzdalifah. They support this with the hadith of Usama ibn Zayd, where the Prophet delayed Maghrib until Muzdalifah, and the statement of Ibn Mas'ud that the two prayers (Maghrib and Fajr) are shifted from their usual times. In contrast, Abu Yusuf holds that the time of Maghrib actually enters at sunset, so if someone prays on the way, the prayer is valid but he has missed the sunnah of praying in Muzdalifah; thus no repetition is required. He cites an athar from Abdullah ibn al-Zubayr that one can pray where Allah has decreed. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: it is wajib to delay Maghrib until Muzdalifah, and if prayed earlier, the prayer is not valid and must be repeated.

Key Terms
سنت (sunnah): In this context, the established practice of the Prophet; praying Maghrib within Muzdalifah is sunnah, not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The prayer is valid and no repetition is needed.
B) The prayer is invalid and must be repeated.
C) The prayer is valid but must be repeated out of caution.
D) The prayer is invalid but no repetition is needed.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, Maghrib prayer on the Day of Arafah must be delayed until Muzdalifah; praying earlier invalidates the prayer, and it must be repeated.

Praying Fajr at Muzdalifah in Darkness
Ruling on performing Fajr prayer early at Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school prescribes praying Fajr in ghalas at Muzdalifah and identify the dalil that supports this exception.

Core Idea
At Muzdalifah, Fajr is prayed in darkness (ghalas) because its time is shifted by nass, overriding the usual sunnah of isfar.

On normal days, the Hanafi school recommends delaying Fajr until twilight (isfar). However, at Muzdalifah on the Day of Sacrifice, the Fajr prayer is performed in complete darkness (ghalas). This exception is based on a hadith from Ibn Mas'ud that explicitly states the prayers of Maghrib and Fajr are shifted from their usual times at this location.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general Hanafi ruling for Fajr timing
State that normally Hanafis consider isfar as sunnah for Fajr.
2
Identify the specific ruling at Muzdalifah
Note that at Muzdalifah, Fajr is to be prayed in ghalas.
3
Locate the dalil
The hadith of Ibn Mas'ud narrated in Bukhari and Muslim.
4
Extract the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet's statement that the two prayers are shifted from their times directly proves the change.
5
Note the thamarah al-khilaf
This ruling applies only to Muzdalifah; on other days the normal ruling remains.

[۶۵۳] (۴۹) فاذا طلع الفجر صلى الامام بالناس الفجر بغلس

عام دنوں میں حنفیہ کے نزدیک نماز فجر اسفار میں پڑھنا سنت ہے لیکن اس دن وقوف مزدلفہ کی وجہ سے اور رمی جمار کی وجہ ہے غلس میں ہی نماز پڑھی جائے گی (۲) عن عبد الرحمن بن يزيد قال خرجت مع عبد الله بن مسعود) الى مكة ثم قد منا جمعا فصلى الـصــلـوتـيـن كل صلوة وحدها باذان واقامة والعشاء بينهما ثم صلى الفجر حين طلع الفجر قائل يقول طلع الفجر وقائل يقول لم يطلع الفجر ثم قال ان رسول الله قال ان هاتين الصلوتين حولنا عن وقتهما في هذا المكان المغرب والعشاء فلا يقدم الناس جمعا حتى يقيموا وصلوة الفجر هذه الساعة (ج) ( بخاری شریف هـستی یصلی الفجر مجمع ص ۲۲۸ نمبر ۱۶۸۳) مسلم شریف ، باب استحباب زيادة الغليس بصلوة اصبح يوم النحر بالمزدلفت ص ۴۲۱۷ نمبر ۱۲۸۹) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مزدلفہ میں صبح کی نماز غلس میں پڑھی جائے گی۔
نوٹ اس حدیث سے یہ بھی معلوم ہوا کہ اس دن نماز فجر کا وقت بدل گیا ہے۔ اس لئے غلس میں نماز پڑھی تو عام دنوں میں اصلی وقت اسفار کے وقت ہے۔ جو حنفیہ کا فجر کی نماز کا سلسلے میں مسلک ہے۔
So when Fajr dawns, the Imam prays Fajr with the people in darkness (ghalas). ... On normal days, according to the Hanafis, it is sunnah to pray Fajr in twilight (isfar), but on this day, because of standing at Muzdalifah and the stoning of the jamarat, the prayer should be in darkness. ... This hadith shows that Fajr at Muzdalifah should be prayed in ghalas. Note: This hadith also shows that the time for Fajr on this day is changed; so if prayed in ghalas, whereas on normal days the proper time is isfar, which is the Hanafi position for Fajr.
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling for Fajr prayer at Muzdalifah on the Day of Sacrifice. The Imam prays Fajr in complete darkness (ghalas), which is an exception to the usual Hanafi practice of praying Fajr in twilight (isfar). The reason is to allow more time for the standing at Muzdalifah (wuquf) and the stoning of the jamarat (rami). The proof is a hadith from Abd al-Rahman ibn Yazid, who accompanied Abdullah ibn Mas'ud at Muzdalifah; Ibn Mas'ud prayed Fajr so early that some doubted whether dawn had truly appeared, and he narrated the Prophet's saying that the two prayers (Maghrib and Fajr) are shifted from their usual times at this place. The commentator notes that this confirms a change in the prayer time for that day. Thus, the Fajr prayer is performed earlier than the usual preferred time, and this is a specific rule for Muzdalifah.

Key Terms
غلس (ghalas): Deep darkness before dawn; the time when Fajr is prayed at Muzdalifah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Standing and Supplication at Muzdalifah After Fajr
Ruling on standing and supplicating at Muzdalifah after Fajr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the post-Fajr standing at Muzdalifah and identify the proof from the hadith of Jabir.

Core Idea
The confirmed sunnah at Muzdalifah is to stand and supplicate after Fajr until asfar, then depart before sunrise.

This passage addresses one of the key rituals of Hajj: the standing at Muzdalifah after Fajr prayer. It clarifies what should be done at that time and when to depart. The ruling is derived from the Prophet's practice as narrated by Jabir. Understanding this confirms the timing and manner of this important sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What exactly is being ruled upon? The act is standing and supplicating at Muzdalifah after Fajr prayer. The ruling is a confirmed sunnah (sunnah muakkadah).
This is not wajib; it is recommended but emphasized.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? The hadith of Jabir ibn Abdullah in Muslim and Abu Dawud describing the Prophet's actions at al-Mash'ar al-Haram.
The hadith is ahad but its meaning is clear.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does this dalil prove the ruling? The phrase 'فلم يزل واقفا حتى اسفر جدا' indicates continuous standing until bright, and 'فدفع قبل ان تطلع الشمس' shows departure before sunrise. This is the Prophet's practice, which is the basis for sunnah.
The Hanafi school takes the Prophet's actions as evidence for sunnah unless it indicates obligation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Does any school disagree? Some other schools may consider this standing as mustahab or even wajib. The Hanafi view is sunnah muakkadah.
The difference does not affect the practical outcome significantly; both agree on the action.

Source Text

ثم وقف الأمام ووقف الناس معه فدعا
پھر امام ٹھہرارہے اور لوگ اس کے ساتھ ٹھہرے رہیں اور دعا کرتے رہیں۔ نماز فجر غلس میں پڑھ کر مزدلفہ ہی میں سب لوگ ٹھہرے رہیں اور اپنے لئے دعا کرتے رہیں۔ کیونکہ طلوع شمس سے پہلے یہاں سے نکلنا ہے تو اس وقت تک دعا اور استغفار کرتے رہے۔ پہلے حدیث گزر چکی ہے جس میں یہ تھا کہ حضور اسفار تک تکبیر وتہلیل کرتے رہے۔ اور دعا کرتے رہے۔ قال دخلنا علی جابر بن عبد الله ... ثم ركب القصواء حتى اتى المشعر الحرام فاستقبل القبلة فدعاه وكبره وهلله ووحده فلم يزل واقفا حتى اسفر جدا فدفع قبل ان تطلع الشمس (الف) ( مسلم شریف، باب حجتہ النبی ص ۳۹۹ نمبر ۱۲۱۸ را بودا اد شریف، باب صفته حجه النبی ص ۲۷۱ نمبر ۱۹۰۵) معلوم ہوا کہ اسفار تک رکبیر تہلیل ، تو حید کرتار ہے اور دعائیں کرتا رہے، اور طلوع ٹس سے قبل مزدلفہ سے منی کے لئے چلے۔
Then the Imam stood and the people stood with him and he supplicated. Then the Imam halts and the people halt with him and continue supplicating. After performing the Fajr prayer in the darkness (ghalas) in Muzdalifah itself, all people continue standing and supplicating for themselves. Because they will leave from here before sunrise, so until that time they engage in supplication and seeking forgiveness. A hadith has passed earlier stating that the Prophet (peace be upon him) continued saying takbir and tahlil until asfar (very bright) and supplicated. He said: We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... then he rode al-Qaswa until he came to al-Mash'ar al-Haram, faced the qibla, and supplicated, saying takbir, tahlil, and tawhid. He continued standing until it became very bright (asfar jiddan), then he departed before sunrise (Reported by Muslim, Bab Hajjat al-Nabi, p.399 no.1218, and Abu Dawud, Bab Sifat Hajjat al-Nabi, p.271 no.1905). It is understood that until asfar he continued takbir, tahlil, tawhid, and supplications, and he left Muzdalifah for Mina before sunrise.
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from the hadith of Jabir. The passage states the ruling that after Fajr prayer in Muzdalifah, both the Imam and the people should stand and engage in supplication until just before sunrise. The proof is the practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) as reported by Jabir: he rode to al-Mash'ar al-Haram, faced the qibla, and continued supplication, takbir, and tahlil until very bright (asfar jiddan), then departed before sunrise. The Urdu commentary emphasizes that the standing is for supplication, and the time for departure is before sunrise, emulating the Prophet's practice.

Key Terms
موقف (mawqif): The place and time of standing during Hajj, specifically at Muzdalifah after Fajr.
اسفار (asfar): The time when the horizon becomes bright, just before sunrise.

All of Muzdalifah is Mawqif Except Batn Muhassir
Specifying the boundary of the standing place at Muzdalifah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the standing place at Muzdalifah, identify the excluded area (Batn Muhassir), and cite the hadith proof.

Core Idea
The entire Muzdalifah is valid for standing except Batn Muhassir, based on the Prophet's explicit command.

In Hajj, the standing (wuquf) at Muzdalifah after Fajr is a sunnah act. This lesson clarifies exactly where a pilgrim may stand, drawing on a clear hadith from Jabir ibn Abdullah. Understanding this boundary ensures the rite is performed correctly and avoids a makruh location.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its subject
The passage states that all of Muzdalifah is a standing place (mawqif) except one specific valley. Determine the act (standing after Fajr) and the general permissibility.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the hadith of Jabir ibn Abdullah cited. Note the exact wording: 'كل المزدلفة موقف وارفعوا عن بطن محسر'. This is the proof for the exception.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
The command 'ارفعوا' (avoid) indicates a prohibition. In Hanafi usul, commands imply obligation but here it is interpreted as makruh tanzih (disliked) because the act is not a pillar of Hajj.
4
Note the historical context
The Urdu commentary mentions that Batn Muhassir is where Allah punished the People of the Elephant. This explains why it is excluded, though the ruling stands on the hadith alone.
5
Apply the ruling in practice
A pilgrim may stand anywhere in Muzdalifah except the valley of Muhassir. If one stands there, the standing is still valid but disliked (makruh).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمزدلفة كلها موقف الا بطن محسر
اور مزدلفہ کل کی کل ٹھہرنے کی جگہ ہے مگر وادی محسر ۔ وادی محسر میں اصحاب فیل والوں کو اللہ نے عذاب دیا تھا اس لئے وادی محسر میں نہ ٹھہرے، وادی محسر مزدلفہ میں ایک وادی کا نام ہے (۲) عن جابر بن عبد الله قال قال رسول الله الله الله كل عرفة موقف وارفعوا عن بطن عرنة و كل المزدلفة موقف وارفعوا عن بطن محسر وكل منى منحر الا ماوراء العقبة (ب) (ابن ماجہ شریف، باب الموقف بفرفات ص ۴۳۶، نمبر ۳۰۱۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مزدلفہ میں بطن محسر ٹھہرنے کی جگہ نہیں ہے۔ باقی جگہ ٹھہر سکتا ہے۔ یوں بھی جب آپ وادی محسر سے گزرے تو اونٹنی کو تیز کر دیا تھا ( نسائی شریف نمبر ۳۰۵۵)
And all of Muzdalifah is a standing place except Batn Muhassir. And the entire Muzdalifah is a place for halting except the valley of Muhassir. Allah punished the People of the Elephant in the valley of Muhassir, so do not halt in the valley of Muhassir. Muhassir is a valley name in Muzdalifah. (2) From Jabir ibn Abdullah: The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'All of Arafah is a standing place, and avoid Batn Aranah; and all of Muzdalifah is a standing place, and avoid Batn Muhassir; and all of Mina is a place of sacrifice except beyond the Aqabah.' (Ibn Majah, Bab al-Mawqif bi 'Arafat, p.436 no.3012) From this hadith it is understood that in Muzdalifah, Batn Muhassir is not a place for halting; the rest of the place one may halt. Also, when the Prophet crossed the valley of Muhassir, he sped up his she-camel (Sunan al-Nasa'i no.3055).
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This is a ruling on the boundaries of the standing place (mawqif) at Muzdalifah. The text states that all of Muzdalifah is a valid place to stand and make supplication, except for the valley of Muhassir (Batn Muhassir). The proof is a hadith from Jabir ibn Abdullah in which the Prophet explicitly says to avoid Batn Muhassir when standing at Muzdalifah. The Urdu commentary adds that this valley is where Allah punished the People of the Elephant, so it is a cursed place; thus one should not halt there. The Prophet also demonstrated this by speeding up when passing through it.

Key Terms
موقف (mawqif): The place where pilgrims stand during the Hajj, specifically at Muzdalifah after Fajr.
بطن محسر (batn muhassir): A valley in Muzdalifah where the People of the Elephant were punished; it is excluded from the standing place.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Departing Muzdalifah Before Sunrise: A Confirmed Sunnah
Ruling on the time of departure from Muzdalifah to Mina

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on the time of departure from Muzdalifah and identify the evidence from the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
Departing Muzdalifah before sunrise is a confirmed sunnah of the Prophet.

After spending the night at Muzdalifah, the pilgrim must proceed to Mina for the stoning ritual. The text clarifies when exactly to set out: before sunrise. This timing is not arbitrary; it is based on the Prophet's explicit action of opposing the polytheists, who waited until the sun had fully risen. In this lesson, we examine the ruling, the evidence, and the wisdom behind this sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is departure (fayd) from Muzdalifah to Mina. The text states it should be before sunrise. The hanafi_position_box classifies this ruling as sunnah muakkadah (confirmed sunnah).
Sunnah muakkadah is a practice the Prophet consistently performed and recommended; omitting it without excuse is blameworthy (makruh tanzih).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is a hadith narrated by 'Umar ibn Maymun, in which 'Umar ibn al-Khattab reports that the polytheists departed after sunrise, but the Prophet (peace be upon him) opposed them and departed before sunrise.
The hadith is from Sahih al-Bukhari, making it a sound (sahih) narration, though it is ahad (single-chain).
3
Understand the rationale (hikmah)
The Prophet's action was an act of opposing the polytheists (mukhalafah), which is a sunnah in itself. This teaches that timing of worship can be a means of distinguishing Islamic practice from other traditions.
The polytheists would say 'Ashriq Thabir' (shine, O Thabir) to signal the start of departure.
4
Apply the ruling in practice
A pilgrim should depart before sunrise. If one delays until after sunrise without a valid excuse, it is makruh tanzih (disliked) but the act remains valid. The Hajj is not invalidated.
Crowd management or safety reasons may justify a slight delay, but one should strive to follow the sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم افاض الامام والناس معه قبل طلوع الشمس حتى ياتو منی
پھر امام اور لوگ ان کے ساتھ سورج طلوع ہونے سے پہلے چلے یہاں تک کہ منی آئے۔ تشریح سورج کے طلوع ہونے سے پہلے مزدلفہ سے منی کے لئے روانہ ہو جائے۔ (۱) مشرکین سورج کے طلوع ہونے کے بعد مزدلفہ سے چلا کرتے تھے۔ لیکن آپ نے ان کی مخالفت کی اور سورج طلوع ہونے سے پہلے وہاں سے منی کے چل پڑے (۲) سمعت عمر بن ميمون يقول شهدت عمر صلى بجمع الصبح ثم وقف فقال ان المشركين كانوا لا يفيضون حتى تطلع الشمس ويقولون اشرق ثبير وان النبي عل خالفهم ثم افاض قبل ان تطلع الشمس (ج) ( بخاری شریف ، باب متی یدفع من جمع ص ۲۲۸ نمبر ۱۶۸۴) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ سورج طلوع ہونے سے پہلے مزدلفہ سے منی کے لئے روانہ ہو۔
Then the Imam and the people with him departed before sunrise until they came to Mina. Then the Imam and the people with him depart before sunrise until they come to Mina. Explanation: He should set out from Muzdalifah to Mina before sunrise. (1) The polytheists used to depart from Muzdalifah after sunrise, but the Prophet opposed them and set out for Mina before sunrise. (2) I heard 'Umar ibn Maymun say: I witnessed 'Umar praying Fajr at Jam' (Muzdalifah) and then stood and said: The polytheists would not depart until the sun had risen, saying 'Shine, Thabir!' but the Prophet (peace be upon him) opposed them and departed before sunrise. (Reported by Bukhari, Bab Mata Yadfa' min Jam', p.228 no.1684) From this hadith it is understood that one should depart from Muzdalifah to Mina before sunrise.
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This is a ruling on the time of departure from Muzdalifah. The text states that the Imam and the pilgrims should depart from Muzdalifah to Mina before sunrise. The proof is the hadith reported by 'Umar ibn Maymun, who saw 'Umar ibn al-Khattab explain that the polytheists used to wait until sunrise to depart, but the Prophet opposed them and departed before sunrise. The Urdu commentary emphasizes that this was an act of opposing the polytheists, and it is sunnah to follow the Prophet's practice.

Key Terms
فيض (fayd): Departure from Muzdalifah to Mina, specifically from the standing place.

The Wajib Manner of Throwing Jamrat al-Aqabah
Ruling with proof on throwing Jamrat al-Aqabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on throwing Jamrat al-Aqabah on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah and identify the prophetic evidence that establishes it.

Core Idea
Throwing Jamrat al-Aqabah is wajib: seven pebbles from the valley bottom, with takbir.

The Day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah) is the climax of Hajj. One of the key rites is the throwing of Jamrat al-Aqabah. The Hanafi school specifies a precise method—seven pebbles, from the bottom of the valley, each thrown with a takbir. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its proof from the Prophet's own Hajj.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled? The throwing of Jamrat al-Aqabah on the 10th. The Hanafi ruling: wajib, not a rukn.
Throwing jamarat is wajib in Hanafi school; omission requires a dam (sacrifice).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Jabir (Muslim, Abu Dawud) describing the Prophet's action on the 10th.
The hadith is ahad, giving zanni thubut but qati dalala.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Prophet threw seven pebbles from the valley bottom, saying takbir. This action establishes the wajib method.
The imperative implication arises from the Prophet's continual practice (fi'l) in the presence of the companions.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Shafi'is consider throwing jamarat a rukn (pillar) of Hajj; Hanafis consider it wajib.
If omitted: Hanafi = dam; Shafi'i = Hajj invalid.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The relied-upon Hanafi position is wajib; a dam is required if omitted or one pebble is missed.
Some early Hanafi opinions considered it a rukn, but the madhhab settled on wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فيبتدأ بجمرة العقبة فيرميها من بطن الوادي بسبع حصيات مثل حصى الخذف
پس جمرہ عقبہ سے شروع کرے اور جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی کرے بطن وادی سے سات کنکری کے ساتھ ٹھیکری کی کنکری کی طرح تین جمرات ہیں۔ اور اس وقت تینوں جگہ سمنٹ کے کھمبے کھڑے ہیں۔ جمرہ اولی، جمرہ وسطی اور عقبہ، دسویں ذی الحجہ کو صرف جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی کرے گا اور بطن وادی سے سات کنکری مارے گا۔ جس طرح ٹھیکرے پھینکتے ہیں اس طرح پھینک کر مارے۔ کھمبے کو لگ جائے تو زیادہ بہتر ہے۔ ورنہ کم سے کم جو چارں طرف تین تین فٹ کے حدود ہیں کنکری اس میں گرے تو کافی ہو جائے گا۔
قال دخـلـنـا عـلـى جابر بن عبد الله ... ثم سلك الطريق الوسطى التى تخرج على الجمرة الكبرى حتى اتى الجمرة التي عند الشجرة فرماها بسبع حصيات يكبر مع كل حصاة منها مثل حصى الخذف رمى من بطن الوادى ثم انصرف الى المنحر (الف) (مسلم شریف ، باب حجتہ النبی ص ۳۹۹ نمبر ۱۲۱۸ ابوداؤد شریف، باب صفته حجتہ النبی ص۲۷۱ نمبر ۱۹۰۵)
He begins with Jamrat al-Aqabah and throws it from the bottom of the valley with seven pebbles like pebbles of khadhf. So he starts with Jamrat al-Aqabah and performs the throwing of Jamrat al-Aqabah from the bottom of the valley with seven pebbles, like the pebbles of a catapult (khadhf). There are three Jamarat. And now there are concrete pillars at all three places: Jamrat al-Ula, Jamrat al-Wusta, and al-Aqabah. On the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, he will only throw at Jamrat al-Aqabah, and he will throw seven pebbles from the bottom of the valley. He should throw them in the manner one throws pebbles. If he hits the pillar, it is better; otherwise, at least the pebbles must fall within the area around it (about three feet on each side). It is reported: We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah... then he took the middle path that leads to the big Jamrat until he came to the Jamrat by the tree, and he threw seven pebbles, saying takbir with each pebble, like pebbles of khadhf, throwing from the bottom of the valley, then he turned to the place of sacrifice. (Muslim, Bab Hajjat al-Nabi, p.399 no.1218; Abu Dawud, Bab Sifat Hajjat al-Nabi, p.271 no.1905).
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This is a ruling on the specific method of throwing Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah). The text states that one should begin with Jamrat al-Aqabah and throw seven pebbles from the bottom of the valley, using pebbles about the size of small stones used in slinging (khadhf). The Urdu commentary explains that there are three jamarat, and on this day only the Aqabah is thrown. The proof is the hadith of Jabir describing the Prophet's Hajj: he threw seven pebbles at the jamrat by the tree, saying takbir with each, from the bottom of the valley, then went to the place of sacrifice.

Key Terms
جمرة العقبة (jamrat al-aqabah): The last (furthest) jamra, located near the Aqabah; the one thrown on 10th Dhul Hijjah.
بطن الوادي (batn al-wadi): The bottom of the valley near Jamrat al-Aqabah.
حصى الخذف (hasa al-khadhf): Small pebbles used for throwing, similar to those used in a slingshot (khadhf).

Saying Takbir with Each Pebble: Sunnah Not Wajib
Ruling on the dhikr during throwing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling of saying takbir during jamarat throwing and explain why it is sunnah rather than wajib based on the Hanafi proof.

Core Idea
Saying takbir with each pebble is sunnah—the Prophet did it, but no command makes it wajib.

This lesson covers the dhikr during the throwing of the jamarat. While throwing each pebble, the Prophet (peace be upon him) would say 'Allahu Akbar'. The text presents this practice and the hadith evidence. We will analyse why the Hanafi school classifies it as sunnah, not wajib.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act under consideration? What ruling does the Hanafi school assign to it?
The act is saying takbir with each pebble during jamarat.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? Identify the hadith and its source.
The hadith of Jabir (Muslim, Abu Dawud) shows the Prophet said takbir with each pebble.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? What is the legal implication of the Prophet's action?
The Prophet's action (fi'l) without a command indicates recommendation (nadb), not obligation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Is there any disagreement among schools? How does the Hanafi position compare?
Some schools consider it mustahab; Hanafis call it sunnah with slight karahah on omission.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
What is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) and why?
Mufta bihi: sunnah; omitting it makes the throw valid but disliked.

D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Saying takbir with each pebble during jamarat is a sunnah practice; its omission does not invalidate the throwing.

Not Standing After Throwing Jamrat al-Aqabah
Ruling on not standing after throwing Jamrat al-Aqabah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on standing after throwing Jamrat al-Aqabah and identify the proof from the practice of Ibn Umar.

Core Idea
Depart immediately after throwing Jamrat al-Aqabah; standing and supplicating is for the other two jamarat only.

This lesson addresses a specific sunnah of Hajj: after throwing the largest Jamrah (Jamrat al-Aqabah), the pilgrim should not halt for supplication but should move on to the next rite. The ruling distinguishes this jamrah from the first and middle ones, where standing and making du'a is recommended. The wisdom behind this is to avoid crowding at that location.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is standing (wuquf) for supplication after throwing Jamrat al-Aqabah. The ruling is that it is sunnah to not stand; one should depart immediately.
The text says 'ولا يقف عندها' (and he does not stand at it).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof cited is the practice of Ibn Umar (radiAllahu anhu) who would throw the first jamrah and say takbir after each pebble. The hadith is partially quoted but supports the general practice.
The full hadith is cut off due to OCR; the Prophet's own action of proceeding directly to sacrifice reinforces this.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The incomplete hadith indicates Ibn Umar's practice; combined with the Prophet's sunnah of not standing, it establishes that standing at Jamrat al-Aqabah is not part of the hajj rites.
The Hanafi school derives that standing is makruh tanzihi (slightly disliked) at this jamrah.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools may allow standing at all jamarat, but the Hanafi view is based on the specific practice to avoid crowding.
The cross-madhhab status is mukhtalaf fih.
5
Apply the ruling in practice
A pilgrim should throw the seven pebbles at Jamrat al-Aqabah, then immediately proceed to slaughter the sacrifice (if qiran or tamattu) or shave/trim hair.
No supplication is made after this jamrah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يقف عندها
اور جمرہ عقبہ کے پاس نہیں ٹھہرے گا۔ تش جمرہ اولی ، جمرہ وسطی پر کنکری مارنے کے بعد ٹھہرے اور دعا کرے لیکن جمرہ عقبہ پر جب بھی کنکریں مارے تو ٹھہرے نہیں بلکہ آگے چلے جائے۔ تا کہ وہاں بھیٹر نہ ہو جائے (۲) حدیث میں ہے عن ابن عمر انه كان يرمى الجمرة الدنيا بسبع حصيات يكبر على اثر
And he does not stand at it. And he will not halt at Jamrat al-Aqabah. Explanation: After throwing at Jamrat al-Ula and Jamrat al-Wusta, one halts and supplicates, but when he throws at Jamrat al-Aqabah at any time, he does not halt but goes ahead. So that there is no crowding there. (2) In the hadith from Ibn Umar that he used to throw the nearest jamrat with seven pebbles, saying takbir after each...
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This is a ruling that distinguishes Jamrat al-Aqabah from the other two jamarat. After throwing at the first and middle jamarat, it is sunnah to stand and make supplication. However, after throwing at Jamrat al-Aqabah, one should not stand but should move forward immediately. The wisdom mentioned in the Urdu commentary is to avoid crowding at that location. The proof is from the practice of Ibn Umar, though the hadith is partially cut off. The general practice of the Prophet, who went straight to the place of sacrifice after throwing Jamrat al-Aqabah, supports this.

Key Terms
وقف (wuquf): To halt and stand for supplication; here it refers specifically to the act of stopping after throwing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
After throwing which jamrah is it sunnah to depart immediately without standing?
A) Jamrat al-Ula
B) Jamrat al-Wusta
C) Jamrat al-Aqabah
D) All of them

Key Takeaway
After throwing Jamrat al-Aqabah, the pilgrim should proceed directly to the next rite without pausing for supplication.

Actions of the Mufrid at Jamrat al-Aqaba on the Day of Nahr
Rulings for the mufrid regarding stoning, talbiyah, and slaughter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five actions of a mufrid at Jamrat al-Aqaba on the Day of Nahr, identify the Hanafi ruling for each (wajib vs. sunnah), and cite the primary hadith evidence.

Core Idea
The mufrid stones Jamrat al-Aqaba from the valley floor, says takbir, does not pause, cuts talbiyah, and may sacrifice.

On the 10th of Dhul Hijjah, the pilgrim performing Hajj Ifrad (mufrid) proceeds to Mina and performs a specific sequence of rites at Jamrat al-Aqaba. This lesson unpacks five rulings from a classical Hanafi commentary, detailing the method of stoning, the recitation of takbir, the prohibition of standing for supplication, the termination of talbiyah, and the discretionary nature of slaughter. Each ruling is grounded in the Prophet's practice as recorded in authentic hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
For each of the five sub-rulings (stoning, takbir, not standing, cutting talbiyah, slaughter), state exactly what the pilgrim does and whether it is wajib (obligatory) or sunnah/mustahabb (recommended) for a mufrid.
Note that slaughter is only mustahabb for the mufrid, while the other four are wajib.
2
Locate the dalil for each ruling
For each act, find the corresponding hadith evidence cited in the passage. The main hadith are from Jabir (stoning method, takbir, slaughter), Ibn Umar (not standing), and Ibn Abbas (cutting talbiyah).
All hadith are authentic (sahih) and from the well-known collections.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how each hadith proves the ruling. For example, the Prophet's practice of throwing from batn al-wadi and saying takbir with each pebble establishes the sunnah; his not standing at Jamrat al-Aqaba after stoning shows that it is not recommended to make du'a there.
The qualification 'if he wishes' in the text for slaughter indicates recommendation, not obligation.
4
Note the condition of the mufrid
Understand that these rulings apply specifically to the mufrid. For tamattu' and qiran, slaughter becomes wajib. Also, the cutting of talbiyah is common to all pilgrims, but the timing may differ between madhahib.
Hanafis cut talbiyah with the first pebble; Shafi'is continue until stoning is complete.
5
Apply the rulings to a practical scenario
Imagine a mufrid on the Day of Nahr. Walk through the steps: he arrives at Jamrat al-Aqaba, stones it from the valley floor with seven pebbles, says takbir each time, does not stop to pray, cuts his talbiyah with the first throw, and optionally slaughters a hady.
Ensure the order is correct: stoning, then slaughter (if desired).

مفرد کے بارے میں چل رہا ہے اور مفرد پر ہدی واجب نہیں ہے بلکہ مستحب ہے اس لئے اگر چاہے تو ہدی ذبح کرے اور چاہے تو نہیں کرے اس لئے مصنف نے فرمایا اگر پسند ہو تو رمی کے بعد ذبح کرے۔ یوں حضور نے ذبح کیا حجتہ النبی ص ۲۹۹ نمبر ۱۲۱۸ ابوداؤد شریف، باب صفته حجته النبی ص ۲۷۱ نمبر ۱۹۰۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ رمی کے بعد مفرد کو ہو سکے تو ذبح کرنا چاہئے۔ یہ ہدی حج کرنے کے شکریہ کے طور پر ہے۔ اس لئے اللہ کا شکر یہ ادا کرنے کے لئے ہدی ذبح کرنا چاہئے۔ حاشیہ : (الف) عبد اللہ بن عمر جمرہ اولی پر رمی فرماتے سات کنکریوں کے ساتھ اور ہر کنکری پر تکبیر کہتے پھر آگے بڑھتے یہاں تک کہ نرم زمین میں آتے پھر قبلہ کا استقبال کر کے کھڑے ہوتے اور دیر تک کھڑے رہتے اور دعا کرتے اور دونوں ہاتھوں کو اٹھاتے پھر جمرہ وسطی کی رمی کرتے پھر بائیں طرف بہتے اور نرم زمین پر جاتے اور قبلہ رخ کھڑے ہوتے پھر دعا کرتے۔ اور ہا تھا ٹھاتے اور دیر تک کھڑے رہتے ۔ پھر جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی کرتے بطن وادی سے اور اس کے پاس نہیں ٹھہرتے ۔ پھر واپس لوٹتے اور فرماتے کہ اس طرح حضور کو کرتے دیکھا ہے (ب) حضور نے فضل ابن عباس کو پیچھے بٹھایا تو انہوں نے خبر دی کہ آپ جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی تک ہمیشہ تکبیر کہتے رہے ( ج ) جب رمی کی تو تلبیہ پڑھنا چھوڑ دیا ( د) پھر آپ مذبح کی طرف واپس لوٹے اور اپنے ہاتھ سے تریسٹھ اونٹ ذبح فرمائے۔ پھر حضرت علی کو دیا اور باقی انہوں نے نحر فرمائے۔ اور حضرت علی کو ہدی میں آپ نے شریک فرمایا۔
Book of Hajj. He comes to Mina [657] (53) He begins with Jamrat al-Aqaba, so he stones it from the bottom of the valley with seven pebbles like pebbles of throwing [258] (54) And he says takbir with each pebble [659] (55) And he does not stand at it. He sets out for Mina. In issue no. 50, the hadith of Sahih Muslim (Muslim no. 1218, Abu Dawud no. 1905) already passed that the Prophet set out for Mina before sunrise. [657] (53) So he should begin with Jamrat al-Aqaba and stone Jamrat al-Aqaba from the bottom of the valley with seven pebbles like pebbles of throwing. There are three jamarat. And now at all three places there are cement pillars. Jamra Ula, Jamra Wusta, and Aqaba. On the 10th of Dhul Hijjah he will only stone Jamrat al-Aqaba and throw seven pebbles from the bottom of the valley. He should throw in the manner of throwing pebbles. It is better if it hits the pillar; otherwise, at least within the boundaries of three feet on all four sides, if the pebble falls within, it will suffice. He said: We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah ... then he took the middle road that leads to the great jamra until he came to the jamra that is by the tree, and he stoned it with seven pebbles, saying takbir with each pebble like pebbles of throwing, he stoned from the bottom of the valley, then he turned to the place of sacrifice. (Muslim, Bab Hajjat al-Nabi p. 399 no. 1218; Abu Dawud, Bab Sifat Hajjat al-Nabi p. 271 no. 1905) From this hadith it is understood that he should throw seven pebbles at Jamrat al-Aqaba from the bottom of the valley. Al-Aqaba: the last, behind. Since it is the last jamra and is behind the two jamarat, it is called Jamrat al-Aqaba. Rami: throwing a pebble. Batn al-Wadi: the name of the place near Jamrat al-Aqaba. Hisat: plural of hisah, pebbles. Al-Khadhf: throwing a piece of pottery. [658] (54) And he says takbir with each pebble. During the stoning of the jamarat, when he throws a pebble, he should say takbir with each pebble. The hadith above passed: yukabbir ma'a kulli hasatin minha (Muslim, p. 399 no. 1218; Abu Dawud no. 1905). The rest of the evidence will come later. [659] (55) And he will not stand at Jamrat al-Aqaba. After stoning Jamra Ula and Jamra Wusta, he should stand and make supplication, but when he stones Jamrat al-Aqaba, he should not stand but move on, so that there is no crowding there. There is a hadith from Ibn Umar: He would stone the first jamra with seven pebbles, saying takbir after each pebble, then he would go forward until he reached soft ground, then stand facing the qibla, stand long, and supplicate and raise his hands. Then he would stone the middle jamra, then take the left side and go to soft ground and stand facing the qibla, stand long and supplicate and raise his hands and stand long. Then he would stone Jamrat al-Aqaba from the bottom of the valley and would not stand at it, then he would depart and say: Thus I saw the Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, do it. (Bukhari, Bab Idha Rama al-Jamratayn Yaqumu Mustaqbil al-Qibla wa Yas'hil p. 236 no. 175) This hadith indicates that he would not stand at Jamrat al-Aqaba. However, after stoning Jamra Ula and Jamra Wusta, he should stand aside and supplicate so as not to inconvenience people. And in this hadith it is also that he would say takbir with each pebble. [260] (56) And he cuts the talbiyah with the first pebble. (57) Then he slaughters if he wishes. And he cuts the talbiyah with the first pebble. There is a hadith from Ibn Abbas: The Prophet, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, seated al-Fadl behind him, and al-Fadl reported that he continued saying the talbiyah until he stoned Jamrat al-Aqaba. (Bukhari, Bab al-Talbiyah wa al-Takbir Ghadat al-Nahr hatta Yarmi al-Jamrat al-Aqaba p. 28 no. 1685) In Ibn Majah there is the addition: When he stoned it, he cut the talbiyah. (Ibn Majah, Bab Mata Yaqta' al-Hajj al-Talbiyah p. 440 no. 3040) From this hadith it is understood that he will recite the talbiyah until Jamrat al-Aqaba, and as soon as he throws the first pebble, he will end the talbiyah. The meaning of talbiyah is 'I am present'. Now to say 'I am present' at the devil would be contrary. Therefore, at the time of stoning the devil, he should end the talbiyah and glorify Allah and say takbir. [261] (57) Then he slaughters if he wishes. Since the discussion is about the mufrid, and for the mufrid, hady is not obligatory but recommended, therefore if he wishes he may slaughter hady, and if he wishes he may not. Thus the author said: if he wishes, then after stoning he slaughters. The Prophet did slaughter. However, if he is doing tamattu' or qiran, then slaughtering is obligatory. There is a hadith: We entered upon Jabir ibn Abdullah ... then he turned to the place of sacrifice and slaughtered sixty-three with his hand, then gave to Ali and he slaughtered the rest, and he made him a partner in his hady. (Muslim, Bab Hajjat al-Nabi p. 299 no. 1218; Abu Dawud, Bab Sifat Hajjat al-Nabi p. 271 no. 1905) From this hadith it is understood that after stoning, if the mufrid is able, he should slaughter. This hady is as a thanksgiving for performing Hajj. Therefore, to express gratitude to Allah, one should slaughter hady. Footnote: (a) Abdullah ibn Umar would stone the first jamra with seven pebbles, saying takbir after each pebble, then go forward until he reached soft ground, then face the qibla and stand long, supplicate, raise his hands, then stone the middle jamra, then go to the left to soft ground, stand facing the qibla, supplicate, raise his hands, stand long, then stone Jamrat al-Aqaba from the bottom of the valley, and not stand at it, then return and say: Thus I saw the Prophet do it. (b) The Prophet seated Fadl ibn Abbas behind him, and he informed that he continued saying takbir until stoning Jamrat al-Aqaba. (c) When he stoned, he stopped reciting the talbiyah. (d) Then he returned to the place of sacrifice and slaughtered sixty-three camels with his hand, then gave to Ali and he slaughtered the rest, and he made Ali a partner in his hady.
Source pages p. 412

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on five consecutive rulings (53-57) from a Hanafi matn (likely Nur al-Idah) regarding the actions of a mufrid (one performing Hajj Ifrad) on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah after arriving at Mina. The author, a Hanafi commentator, explains each ruling with Urdu glosses and supports them with hadith from the Prophet's Hajj.

Ruling (53): The pilgrim must begin stoning with Jamrat al-Aqaba (the large jamra) on the Day of Sacrifice. He should stone it from the bottom of the valley (batn al-wadi) with seven pebbles, each approximately the size of a chickpea (like pebbles used for throwing, i.e., small stones). The commentator clarifies that there are three jamarat: al-Ula (first), al-Wusta (middle), and al-Aqaba (the last). Currently, concrete pillars mark each spot. On the 10th, only Jamrat al-Aqaba is stoned. The stoning is valid if the pebble lands within the designated area (approx. 3 feet radius around the pillar), though hitting the pillar is better.

Ruling (54): While throwing each pebble, the pilgrim says 'Allahu Akbar' (takbir). This is proven from the hadith of Jabir and Ibn Umar.

Ruling (55): After stoning Jamrat al-Aqaba, the pilgrim should not stop to make supplication. However, after stoning the other two jamarat (on subsequent days), he should move aside and make lengthy supplication facing the qibla, as per the practice of Ibn Umar. The reason is to avoid crowding and because the Prophet did not stand at Jamrat al-Aqaba.

Ruling (56): The pilgrim cuts his talbiyah (the chant 'Labbayk Allahumma Labbayk') as soon as he throws the first pebble at Jamrat al-Aqaba. This is based on Ibn Abbas's hadith that the Prophet continued talbiyah until he stoned Jamrat al-Aqaba, and the addition in Ibn Majah that he stopped upon stoning. The commentator explains the wisdom: at the devil, one should not say 'I am present' but rather glorify Allah.

Ruling (57): After stoning, the mufrid may optionally slaughter a sacrificial animal (hady). This is mustahabb (recommended), not wajib, because the mufrid is not obligated to offer hady unlike the mutamatti' or qarin. The Prophet slaughtered 63 camels on that day. The hady is an expression of gratitude for completing Hajj.

All rulings are supported by authentic hadith from Bukhari, Muslim, Abu Dawud, and Ibn Majah. The commentary ensures the student understands the precise Hanafi positions and the evidence.

Key Terms
جمرة العقبة (Jamrat al-Aqaba): The last of the three stone pillars (jamarat) in Mina, stoned on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah and subsequent days. It is located near the 'Aqaba (the mountain pass).
بطن الوادي (Batn al-Wadi): The bottom or middle of the valley, specifically the area near Jamrat al-Aqaba where the Prophet stood and stoned from.
رمي (Ramy): Throwing pebbles at the jamarat during Hajj. Each pebble must be thrown, not placed or dropped.
حصيات (Hisat (pl. of Hisah)): Small pebbles used for stoning, approximately the size of a chickpea (like those used for throwing in khadhf).
تلبية (Talbiyah): The chant 'Labbayk Allahumma Labbayk...' recited by the pilgrim from the start of ihram until stoning Jamrat al-Aqaba on the 10th.
هدي (Hady): A sacrificial animal offered in the precincts of the Haram during Hajj. For the mufrid it is optional (mustahabb).
نحر (Nahr): Slaughtering a camel by cutting the jugular vein at the base of the neck. The Day of Nahr is the 10th of Dhul Hijjah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Wajib (obligatory)
B) Sunnah (recommended)
C) Haram (forbidden)
D) Mubah (permissible but not recommended)

Key Takeaway
A mufrid's actions at Jamrat al-Aqaba on the Day of Nahr consist of stoning from the valley floor with seven pebbles, saying takbir, not standing, cutting talbiyah at the first throw—all wajib—and optional slaughter as a recommended act of gratitude.

Cutting Talbiyah at Jamrat al-Aqabah
Ruling with direct hadith evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on cutting talbiyah during hajj and identify the hadith evidence that establishes it as a sunnah practice.

Core Idea
Talbiyah ends with the first stone at Jamrat al-Aqabah, not after the farewell tawaf.

In this lesson, we examine a clear ruling from the Hanafi school: the pilgrim cuts the talbiyah (labbayk) at the moment of stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah. The source provides both the matn (ruling statement) and the hadith proof, helping you connect the ruling to its evidence. Understanding this timing ensures your hajj rituals follow the sunnah precisely.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The source states that the pilgrim cuts the talbiyah 'with the first pebble' at Jamrat al-Aqabah. This is the act being ruled upon. Determine whether it is fard, wajib, or sunnah based on the Hanafi classification.
The ruling level is sunnah muakkadah.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites Hadith from Ibn Abbas: the Prophet continued talbiyah until stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah (Bukhari) and an addition from Ibn Majah that upon stoning, he cut the talbiyah.
The dalil is a Sunan (Prophetic action).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith directly shows the Prophet's action: he stopped talbiyah immediately after the first stone. This action (fi'l) indicates a recommended practice (sunnah) unless there is evidence of obligation.
In Hanafi usul, the Prophet's action can indicate sunnah or obligation depending on context. Here it is sunnah.
4
Note the wisdom (hikmah)
The commentator explains that talbiyah means 'I am present (in response to Your call)' and saying that at the shaytan is inappropriate. Instead, one should glorify Allah (takbir) while stoning.
This wisdom reinforces the ruling's suitability.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof that the talbiyah (labbayk) is terminated with the first stone thrown at Jamrat al-Aqabah on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah. The matn states: 'He cuts the talbiyah with the first pebble.' The commentator explains that this is based on the hadith of Ibn Abbas, where the Prophet continued saying labbayk until he stoned the Jamrat al-Aqabah, and the addition in Ibn Majah explicitly states that upon stoning, he cut the talbiyah. The wisdom is that talbiyah is a response to Allah's call for the hajj, which is fulfilled with the stoning; thereafter, one should glorify Allah (takbir) instead of continuing the talbiyah. This is a sunnah practice in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms

حصاة (hasah): A pebble used for stoning the jamarat.
جمرة العقبة (jamrat al-aqabah): The largest of the three stoning pillars, stoned on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah.

The talbiyah is sunnah muakkadah and is cut at the very first pebble thrown at Jamrat al-Aqabah on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah.
