نے فرمایا جب تیر ہو میں ذی الحجہ کو دن پھوٹ پڑے تو رمی کرنا بھی حلال اور واپس جانا بھی حلال ہے نوٹ : یوم النفر الآخر تیرہویں ذی الحجہ کو کہتے ہیں (ج) حضور کو دیکھا کہ دسویں تاریخ کو چاشت کے وقت اپنی سواری پر رمی کر رہے تھے ۔ اور دسویں ذی الحجہ کے بعد تو زوال شمس کے بعد رمی کرتے۔
If he advances the stoning on this day before zawal after the appearance of fajr, it is permissible according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said it is not permissible. That is, on the 11th and 12th days, after stoning the jamarat, he may return. There is a narration from Ibn Umar: he used to say, 'Whoever has the sun set upon him while he is in Mina in the middle of the days of Tashriq, he should not depart until he stones the jamarat the next day.' (a) From Ibn Abbas, he said: 'When the day breaks on the last day of departure (yawm al-nafr al-akhir), then stoning and departing are permissible.' (b) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on whoever has the sun set on him on the first day of departure in Mina... 5:1248, numbers 9687/9686) From this hadith it is understood that if the evening of the 12th comes, he should not depart from Mina, but rather on the 13th after zawal he should stone and then return. (174) (70) So if on this day (the 13th) he performs the stoning before zawal but after the appearance of fajr, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa it is permissible, and the Sahibayn said it is not permissible. On the 13th of Dhul Hijjah, if he wishes to stone before zawal and after sunrise, according to Imam Abu Hanifa it is permissible, and according to the Sahibayn it is not permissible. (1) When there is allowance that he may not stone on the 13th at all, then there will also be allowance that he stone before zawal. (2) The athar mentioned above from Ibn Abbas: 'When the day breaks on the last day of departure, stoning and departing are permissible.' (Sunan al-Bayhaqi...) In this hadith, it is said that when the day breaks, stoning becomes halal. And 'the day breaks' means the rising of the sun. So after sunrise, he may stone if he wishes on the 13th. The Sahibayn say that on the 13th he should stone after zawal as well, because the hadith states that on the 10th the Prophet stoned after sunrise, and on the remaining days after zawal. The hadith: 'I heard Jabir ibn Abdullah say: I saw the Messenger of Allah on his mount on the day of Nahr in the forenoon, but after that it was after zawal.' (c) (Abu Dawud, chapter on stoning the jamarat, p. 278, no. 197) From this hadith it is understood that on the 10th of Dhul Hijjah he stones after sunrise, and after that on the remaining days he used to stone after zawal. This implies that on the 13th of Dhul Hijjah he would also stone after zawal. Imam Abu Hanifa became inclined to stoning after sunrise due to the saying of Abdullah ibn Abbas. Footnote: (a) Ibn Umar said: In the middle of the days of Tashriq (i.e., the 12th of Dhul Hijjah), whoever has the sun set on him in Mina, he should not depart until he stones on the next day, i.e., the 13th. (b) Ibn Abbas said: When the day breaks on the 13th of Dhul Hijjah, then stoning is permissible and departing is also permissible. Note: Yawm al-nafr al-akhir is called the 13th of Dhul Hijjah. (c) I saw the Prophet on the 10th stoning in the forenoon on his mount, and after the 10th he used to stone after zawal.
Source pages p. 419

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute (between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn) and also a ruling with evidence. The issue is the timing of stoning the jamarat on the 13th of Dhul Hijjah. According to Abu Hanifa, it is permissible to stone before zawal (midday) but after fajr (dawn) on the 13th, whereas Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad require stoning after zawal, as on the other days of Tashriq. The text presents the evidence for each side. For Abu Hanifa: the saying of Ibn Abbas that on the day of 'nafr al-akhir' (13th), stoning becomes halal at the break of dawn (i.e., sunrise). He also uses a rational argument (qiyas): since stoning on the 13th is not obligatory (one may leave on the 12th), doing it before zawal should also be permissible. For the Sahibayn: the established practice of the Prophet (peace be upon him) is that on the 10th he stoned after sunrise, and on all subsequent days (11th, 12th, 13th) he stoned after zawal. This is based on the hadith of Jabir. The Sahibayn also rely on the saying of Ibn Umar that if the sun sets on the 12th while one is in Mina, he must stay and stone on the 13th after zawal. The commentator explains that Abu Hanifa's view is based on the literal meaning of Ibn Abbas's statement that stoning is permissible from dawn, while the Sahibayn follow the general practice of the Prophet. The passage does not definitively state which view is mufta bihi, but the discussion shows the strength of both arguments.

Key Terms
رمي (ramy): Stoning the jamarat by throwing pebbles at the pillars in Mina.
زوال (zawal): The time when the sun passes its zenith, i.e., midday.
يوم النفر الآخر (yawm al-nafr al-akhir): The last day of departure from Mina, which is the 13th of Dhul Hijjah.
صاحبین (Sahibayn): The two companions of Abu Hanifa: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, why must stoning on the 13th of Dhul Hijjah be performed after zawal?
A) Because the hadith of Ibn Abbas explicitly says so.
B) Because the Prophet stoned after zawal on all days after the 10th, as reported by Jabir.
C) Because stoning before zawal is a sin.
D) Because the Sahibayn rejected the hadith of Ibn Abbas.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school contains a legitimate disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the timing of stoning on the 13th, with the practical consequence that stoning before zawal is valid according to one view and invalid according to the other.
